Xue Dubi Returned to Shanghai from Beijing Yesterday Morning

Talked about Feng Yuxiang Going to Guangdong, Said He Had Not Heard of It; Li Zongren Definitely Intends to Come North

Central Committee member Xue Dubi went to Beijing a few days ago to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee. Now that the plenary session has ended, he took the night train from Beijing to Shanghai on the evening of the 11th and arrived at the North Station at 7:15 yesterday morning. He immediately returned to his residence on Masnan Road to rest. Then, he met with reporters from various newspapers and made the following remarks.

Good Impression: According to Xue, the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee was held in Beijing this time, and the impression was exceptionally good. Since 1928, the number of attendees at the plenary session has been the largest this year, because there is no way to save the country without national unity. Although there were few proposals at this plenary session, all the Central Committee members were able to concentrate and study them in detail, and they will be implemented one by one in the future.

Feng Staying in Beijing: Mr. Feng Huanzhang has now decided to stay in Beijing for a long time. Mrs. Feng has also arrived in Beijing from Shandong. If there is an opportunity in the future, Feng plans to visit various places to inspect the construction situation in various provinces. As for the rumor of going to Guangdong, it has not been heard in Beijing, and I am afraid it is not accurate.

Li Will Come North: Mr. Dai Jitao and Mr. Ma Chaojun went south this time to exchange opinions, and the results were quite satisfactory. The Southwest will send several people to Beijing to attend the Fifth National Congress. The plan for the National Assembly is that the candidates from the North have not been heard of yet. Mr. Li Zongren definitely intends to come north, but the date of departure has not been decided.

Meeting of the Issuance Reserve Management Committee Held Yesterday

Standing Committee Members Including Song Ziwen and Xu Dong Meet with Finance Minister Kong to Report

Following the Ministry of Finance's announcement of the new monetary policy and its implementation nationwide, the financial situation in various regions has gradually stabilized. The Issuance Reserve Management Committee, responsible for overseeing the issuance, continued its Standing Committee meeting yesterday morning, after which they met with Finance Minister Kong to report on the various regulations for managing the reserve fund. It is expected that these regulations will be announced and implemented within a few days. A summary of the situation is as follows:

Reserve Committee Holds Standing Committee Meeting. The Issuance Reserve Management Committee, which supervises the issuance by the three banks, held a Standing Committee meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday in the Board of Directors' office on the third floor of the Central Bank. Standing Committee members Song Ziwen, Chen Guangfu, Hu Bijiang, Qian Xinzhi, and Li Jue were present. Drafting committee members Xu Kan, Zhang Gongquan, and others were also in attendance. Mr. Xu presented the draft regulations prepared by the drafting committee, which were discussed in detail. The plan is to convene a full committee meeting to pass the regulations and submit them to the ministry for implementation. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

Xu Kan and Chen Xing Meet with Finance Minister Kong. Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi left Beijing the night before and arrived in Shanghai around 7:00 AM on the 7th. After returning to his residence to rest, he went to the Central Bank around 11:00 AM to handle official business. Xu Kan and Chen Xing immediately met with Mr. Kong to report on the progress of drafting the various regulations and to seek his instructions. It is said that the draft operational regulations include several items, such as measures for the custody of the reserve fund, methods for the exchange of legal tender, and regulations for the inspection of the reserve fund.

Investigation of Bank Reserves Continues Yesterday. The Issuance Reserve Committee has been dispatching personnel to various issuing banks since the day before yesterday to investigate the amount of issuance and reserves (excluding the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications). Ye Zhuotang and others have completed their investigation of banks such as Zhejiang Industrial Bank. Yesterday morning, they continued their investigation at banks such as China Industrial Bank, completing it in the evening. It is reported that once the investigation of the reserve amount of each bank is completed, the Reserve Committee will notify each bank to transfer the reserve fund to the central, Chinese and Communications Reserve Depository for safekeeping. Although the banknotes already issued by the banks are still allowed to circulate, they are not allowed to continue issuing after the new system is implemented. The exchange of old banknotes will be handled by the Reserve Committee.

The Foreign Exchange Market is Very Stable

Yesterday morning, the Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee announced the equalization tax rate as 57.25%. The Central Bank announced the foreign exchange rates as follows: London one shilling and two and a half pence (equivalent to one yuan in national currency), New York 29.75 yuan, Berlin 73.5 marks, Paris 450 francs, Japan 103 yuan, Hong Kong 80 yuan (all above rates are per 100 yuan in national currency). Customs gold is equivalent to 2.276 yuan in national currency, 33 pence in British gold, and 67.75 cents in American gold per yuan. The rates were the same as in previous days and differed very little from the rates quoted by HSBC. After the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications made every effort to sell foreign exchange to regulate the market, the exchange market has become very stable.

Special Margin for Gold Market Cancelled. The Shanghai Gold Exchange, due to the sharp rise in gold prices a week ago, had announced the collection of a special margin of 50 yuan per tael. Now that the new system has been implemented, financial stability has been achieved, and the upward trend has disappeared. Prices are now below 1,150 yuan. Therefore, an announcement was issued yesterday canceling the special margin. As market prices are gradually stabilizing, the special margin will be canceled from today. Only the original margin of 50 yuan in legal tender per tael will be required. This announcement is hereby made.

Full Cash Exchange for Legal Tender. After the Ministry of Finance announced that silver could no longer be used, it immediately sent personnel to various banks and the joint reserve of money shops to investigate the silver reserves and ordered them to be exchanged for legal tender. The Central Bank also sent letters to various foreign banks instructing them to submit their silver deposits for exchange for legal tender. The regulation for exchanging legal tender stipulates that one yuan of silver is exchanged for one yuan of legal tender, or silver is converted at a rate of 71.5%. It must be at full value. For example, the money shops previously sent more than one million yuan of silver from their reserves to the three banks for exchange for legal tender, all at full value. Reuters Shanghai, 7th: The Governor of the Central Bank today denied the rumor that 60% of silver and 40% of other securities could be exchanged for banknotes of government banks, saying that the three banks controlled by the government are now issuing banknotes at a rate of one yuan of paper money for one yuan of silver. He also said that all silver dollars held by various institutions and banks, including the three government banks, are now being taken over by the Issuance Reserve Management Committee without any deductions.

Premium on Hong Kong Dollars in Guangdong Expected to Increase Significantly. National News Agency, Shanghai, 7th: A well-known foreign exchange banker in the city told a reporter from the National News Agency that the premium on Hong Kong dollars in Guangdong is expected to increase significantly. However, this is not surprising. Firstly, because the Guangdong Provincial Government has only now begun to implement a ban on the export of silver. Secondly, the Guangzhou dollar is often 25 cents less than the central silver dollar.

Shanghai General Labor Union Sends Telegram in Support. The Shanghai General Labor Union, believing that the Ministry of Finance's resolute reform of the currency system this time will benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday to express its support. The text of the telegram is as follows (titles omitted): Since the global economic crisis in recent years, countries have successively revised their monetary policies, leading to a surge in silver prices. As a silver-using country, we have been the first to bear the brunt of the impact. The huge trade deficit and the outflow of large amounts of silver have caused domestic currency to contract, and the national economy has been declining day by day. The entire financial foundation has been on the verge of collapse, and the industrial and commercial sectors have been withering, unemployment has been increasing, and people have been anxious, feeling that the situation cannot continue. The Ministry deeply knows that if it does not seek urgent solutions, the silver will inevitably flow out completely, and the consequences will be unimaginable. Therefore, it has acted bravely and decisively and resolutely announced the reform of the currency system and the implementation of currency management. The news has spread, and the people are rejoicing, and it is expected that financial stability and smooth currency circulation will be achieved in the future, and the prosperity of the market and the revival of industry and commerce can be expected. The Union respectfully represents all the workers in Shanghai in expressing unanimous support. Respectfully, the Shanghai General Labor Union.

He Bingxian Hopes for National Support. Central News Agency: This time, the new monetary policy implemented by our government has a great impact on our country's foreign trade. The reporter specially visited Mr. He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, to seek his opinion. He provided detailed answers as follows: The new monetary policy promulgated by the government this time is closely related to our country's foreign trade. The major aspects are as follows: (1) As a result of our country's implementation of the new monetary system, exchange rates can tend to stabilize, and at the same time, the domestic price level is expected to be balanced with foreign price levels. Those engaged in foreign trade no longer need to bear the risk of exchange rate fluctuations. Therefore, import and export trade can be expected to be stable and developed, sweeping away the impact of exchange rate speculation in the past. (2) After stabilizing the foreign exchange rate of the national currency, our country's exchange rate will be lowered, and the prices of our country's goods in foreign markets will be cheaper. Therefore, export trade is expected to increase. Conversely, in terms of imports, the prices of imported goods may be higher. (3) The stability of the currency can attract foreign capital inflows to seek the revival of the domestic economy. At the same time, our country does not need to immediately repay the import goods from various countries, but can keep them in our country to earn interest or engage in investment. In this way, our country's trade deficit can be compensated, and capital outflow can be gradually avoided. (4) As a result of the implementation of the new monetary policy, prices will tend to rise, so agriculture, industry, and commerce can gradually prosper. On the one hand, people's purchasing power will increase, and on the other hand, export capacity will increase. If a comprehensive calculation can be made, it will not be difficult to achieve a mutually adaptable increase in import and export trade, and our country's position in international commerce can also be improved. (5) Since foreign exchange is purchased and sold by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications without any restrictions, it will naturally generate an adjustment function for our country's import and export trade. In this way, our country's foreign trade will be brought back on track in the future. In short, the monetary policy promulgated by the government this time is the best policy for revitalizing our country's foreign trade. We only hope that the people of the country will support it unanimously so that we can achieve prosperity together.

Various Industries Separately Stabilize Commodity Prices. Since the Ministry of Finance promulgated the implementation of legal tender, the chips have been able to move and revival is expected. Industrial and commercial circles are all pleased. The Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association specially convened a meeting of all members yesterday to discuss various issues to cope with the environment. Representatives from 37 employee factories attended, chaired by Hu Xituan and recorded by Lin Chao. There were detailed discussions on issues such as raw material financing and commodity prices, and in particular, a more detailed study was made on stabilizing commodity prices. It is reported that other industries will also hold meetings separately to discuss issues such as stabilizing commodity prices.

Sir Ross Gives a Talk. The China Press reports that rumors circulating abroad that the currency system recently announced by the Chinese government was the result of an agreement with the United Kingdom to borrow money have been firmly denied by Sir Ross, the Chief Economic Advisor to the British government. He has also allowed overseas newspapers to publish his statement. The Japanese envoy, Arimasa, based on this denial, gave a talk on the 2nd of October. Sir Ross acknowledged that he had discussed the possibility of borrowing money with the Japanese and American ambassadors. However, Sir Ross told the China Press yesterday (6th) that the Chinese government was forced by market conditions to resolutely implement the new currency system without waiting for the guarantee of loans from various countries. However, for a country in China's position, borrowing money would be very beneficial, and he hoped that in the future, it would be possible to negotiate a solution through the cooperation of other countries, including Japan. Sir Ross then reiterated the Chinese government's monetary plan, saying that, on the whole, this move was not surprising, as abandoning the silver standard had long been expected by the general public. What is surprising is that it was launched suddenly without external assistance. This move is based on the principle of self-reliance, and he hoped that it would be fully successful. The reserves now held by the three banks are sufficient for the government to cope with the situation comfortably. Gradually, China will be in a better position in import and export trade. For the success of the new plan, the reform of the banking system, especially the establishment of an independent central reserve bank, is essential. He had discussed this with the Chinese government and regarded it as part of any monetary plan. The Chinese government has now begun to implement it, which is gratifying.

American Banking Circles Are Very Willing to Cooperate. American Ambassador Johnson told a representative of the China Press yesterday (6th) that he had no comments to make at present regarding the attitude of the American government towards the currency reform implemented by the Chinese government. Johnson has gone to Beijing yesterday and plans to return to Shanghai at the end of the month. Other American government officials stationed in Shanghai said that only the ambassador can express opinions on this issue if it is necessary to make any comments. According to reports, there are three American banks with branches in Shanghai, namely Citibank, Chase Bank, and American Express Bank. It is reported that all three banks reported everything to their head offices yesterday. Mr. Mackay, Vice President of Citibank, said that Citibank is very willing to cooperate with the Chinese government on the currency reform in China, but Washington must provide appropriate protection.

Commemoration of the Anniversary of Martyr Xia's Sacrifice

Solemn Family Sacrifice Held.

Heroic Deeds of the Martyr.

Central News Agency: Yesterday was the 20th anniversary of the martyrdom of General Xia Renqing. Xia Xiaoxia, the son of Martyr Xia, specially came to Shanghai from Beijing the night before and held a family sacrifice. Many relatives and friends came to pay their respects, and the situation was quite solemn. Mr. Xia was an advanced member of the Party and the country. He supported the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, organized the Chinese Revolutionary Party, and worked hard for the revolution. He made great contributions. In 1915, he was martyred at No. 1 Hongyi Lane, Pobo Road, French Concession, Shanghai. The deeds of Martyr Xia are recorded below. Xia Zhiqi, styled Renqing, was from Qingtian County, Zhejiang Province. At the age of seventeen, he was selected to enter the Jiangnan Military Academy. After graduation, he served successively as an instructor at the Wusong Fort, a training officer in the Jiangxi Standing Army, an instructor at the Jiangxi Military Academy, an instructor at the Nanjing Military Research Institute, a supervisor at the Anhui Training Office, a superintendent of the Jiangxi Army Primary School, and the head of the Jiangxi Military Academy. In Anhui, he met Xu Xilin, Xiong Chengji, and other comrades. He advocated revolution, contacted comrades, and served in education for a total of fifteen years. He was well-known wherever he went. Active military officers who came from his school include Li Liejun, Xiong Shihui, Cao Haosen, and Zhou Hunyuan. During the Wuchang Uprising, Jiujiang responded. At that time, the martyr was serving as the superintendent of the Jiangxi Army Primary School. He summoned the students to encourage them with great righteousness. He personally supervised and led the students, united with the standard battalion artillery team, and attacked and captured the Fuzhou government. He was recommended by the public as the temporary governor, but he declined and recommended Wu Jiezhang to take the post. He himself took charge of military affairs. In March of the Republic of China, Li Liejun was appointed governor of Jiangxi. He sent telegrams to urge and invite him. Due to the friendship between teacher and student, he strongly declined but could not refuse. He returned to take charge of the Military Academy and also served as a senior advisor. In March of the second year of the Republic of China, the Yuan government borrowed 25 million pounds of foreign debt in the name of good settlement. Coincidentally, the Song case broke out suddenly. The martyr knew that Yuan Shikai would revive the ashes of autocracy and betray the trust of the people. Li Liejun came to Shanghai to contact five provinces and planned a second revolution. He appointed the martyr as the chief of staff and rushed back to Hukou to declare war on Yuan Shikai. At that time, the northern soldiers were stationed everywhere, and Li Chun and Duan Zhigui also went south. However, the two provinces of Zhejiang and Fujian were still watching and not moving forward, resulting in failure. The martyr's calculations returned to nothing. Later, Yuan Shikai dissolved the National Assembly, established the Senate, and abolished provincial autonomy. The martyr went to Japan to support Mr. Sun Yat-sen and organized the Chinese Revolutionary Party, urgently planning a third revolution. The public believed that Yuan's power was strong and wanted to wait, but he insisted that it was not possible. He returned to Shanghai to contact comrades. In April of the third year of the Republic of China, the martyr went to Japan again and, under the orders of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, returned from Japan with Chen Qimei, Zhu Zhixin, Ju Zheng, Xu Chongzhi, Shi Qingyang, Fan Mingxian, and other comrades. He was assigned military affairs in Zhejiang, Shanghai, Guangdong, Fujian, Shandong, and Sichuan provinces. The martyr was ordered to be the Director of Military Affairs, focusing on Zhejiang. The Zhejiang officials detected it and sent Wang Donglu and others to Shanghai to persuade him. The martyr calmly declined and said, "You gentlemen are planning for me very well, but shouldn't I plan for my 400 million compatriots?" Wang and others were speechless and left. As a result, the Zhejiang officials became more vigilant, and the martyr's determination became stronger. He set up agencies everywhere in Hangzhou and decided to launch an uprising on November 24th of that year. One day before, the matter was leaked, and more than 30 comrades died or were imprisoned. At that time, the Qingdao war was urgent, and he was even more indignant. He vowed to raise a different army and go to Japan again to discuss the progress. In the spring of the fourth year of the Republic of China, under the orders of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, he was appointed Director of Military Affairs in Jiangxi. Xia Ciyan was appointed to take charge of Zhejiang affairs. Before long, Xia Ciyan went to Japan, and he took charge of Zhejiang affairs himself. As a result, new and old comrades gathered and competed to be under his command, and his influence grew day by day. The agencies in the two provinces were destroyed and rebuilt, and those who died for the country followed one another without complaint. The martyr always treated people with frankness and without suspicion, so the soldiers were happy to be used by him. At that time, the spies from Jiangxi and Zhejiang came to Shanghai, and Yuan Shikai offered 100,000 gold to buy the martyr. Xiang Lan, who was greedy for money, took the opportunity to assassinate him. He was seriously injured and died. The martyr was only thirty-eight years old at the time.

Shipping Industry Submits to Sixth Plenary Session: Requesting Expedited Issuance of Shipping Industry Public Bonds

Private Shipping Industry in Dire Straits: Inaction is Doomed

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association submitted a report to the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, detailing the decline of the shipping industry and requesting approval for the issuance of public bonds worth ten million yuan. The original report is excerpted below:

Detailing Difficulties, Seeking Assistance

The submission is regarding the private shipping industry, which is in dire straits. The current situation is unsustainable and on the verge of collapse. We respectfully present the various points of difficulty, and beseech your esteemed committee to review and grant swift assistance. We believe that the shipping industry bears a significant mission and has a profound relationship with the nation, unlike other commercial enterprises. It should be valued by the government, with the hope that it will be safeguarded and nurtured. Our nation's private shipping industry is inherently immature, coupled with the fact that the capital of those engaged in this business is often insufficient. In the past, during periods of smooth transportation, they could barely maintain themselves, with little capacity for development. In recent years, due to frequent turbulent times and repeated disasters, they have suffered repeated blows, injuring their vitality. More recently, due to the recession in all industries, transportation has decreased, and the number of ships without cargo loading and ceasing navigation has been increasing daily. Shipping merchants are facing difficult times, business is declining, loans are impossible to obtain, and they are at the end of their rope, unable to survive. If this continues, the private shipping industry will be seen to collapse beyond recovery, and its future is truly lamentable. We now specifically present to your esteemed committee the most difficult points currently facing us.

Restricting Shipping Routes Causes Disputes

(1) There are no restrictive regulations on the routes that ships can travel in advanced shipping nations. They are mostly divided into three types—ocean-going, coastal, and inland river—based on the condition and capacity of the ships themselves. There is no listing of the names of each port. Currently, ships in our country must list the names of each location on their shipping route certificate. If a location is not listed, they are not allowed to travel there. The original intention of this legislation was likely due to the unequal treaties our country was subjected to, which allowed foreign ships to travel freely inland, so the names of locations were listed to slightly restrict them. Unexpectedly, foreign ships are now not subject to this restriction. They only need a letter from their respective consuls to freely set sail, while only our nation's shipping merchants are subject to this constraint. Shipping merchants are already spending a lot of time and money being bound by this restriction. Recently, the Ministry of Transportation, which is in charge of the shipping industry, has issued an order regarding several inland port routes: "Maintain the status quo before the announcement of the shipping industry reorganization plan." All ships, whether they have a shipping route certificate or not, are not allowed to join in operation. Although the purpose is to quell disputes, the supply and demand are not aligned, the disparity between prosperity and hardship is increasing, and disputes are instead being caused by this. This is the first difficulty.

State-Run and Private Compete Against Each Other

(2) Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was taken over by the state, the shipping industry has been divided into state-run and private. The government's establishment of state-owned shipping and the simultaneous encouragement and protection of private shipping are both clearly stipulated in the Provisional Constitution. However, there are no regulations for division of labor and cooperation between state-run and private, and there is already a reality of competition against each other. State-run companies have priority and exclusive access to all due rights, while private companies bear more of the obligations. If this continues, the recovery of shipping rights will be indefinite, and the bankruptcy of private shipping is imminent. This is the second difficulty.

Water-Land Intermodal Transportation Should Not Be Monopolized

(3) Water-land intermodal transportation between railways and ships facilitates the transfer of goods and is related to the connection of transportation. All countries have implemented it long ago. In our country, since the pilot implementation in the 22nd year of the Republic, private companies have repeatedly requested to participate equally, but the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has always intended to monopolize it. After the Ministries of Transportation and Railways reviewed and approved participation, they continued to delay and obstruct it in every way. Therefore, although approval has been granted for more than a year, private companies have not yet benefited from it. This is the third difficulty.

Tonnage Surcharge and Additional Donations: Unable to Continue Bearing the Burden

(4) The Ministry of Transportation re-established the Wusong Merchant Marine School. Because the costs of restoration were high and the national budget was insufficient to include it, officials were sent to negotiate with merchants. For the sake of cultivating talent and regaining national rights, shipping merchants reluctantly agreed to shoulder 30% of the tonnage surcharge and additional donations to facilitate its completion. This was originally a temporary expedient measure. However, from the 18th year of the Republic to the present, it has continued for six years, amounting to more than 100,000 yuan per year. Since foreign merchant ships do not bear this burden, it has already become difficult in comparison. Recently, they are finding it hard to take care of themselves, and are truly unable to continue bearing this burden. The national education budget has a large annual expenditure, and it should not be difficult to include this only national merchant marine school in the budget. Repeated submissions to the Ministry of Transportation have not been approved to cease the levy. This is the fourth difficulty.

Shipping Industry Public Bonds Should Be Issued Quickly

(5) In the 19th year of the Republic, shipping merchants, due to business depression and financial distress, submitted a request to the government to issue 10 million yuan in shipping industry public bonds to provide relief. The plan was to use the ships as collateral for low-interest loans, and after ten years, the funds would be used to develop international shipping routes. However, although approval was granted, the issuance has been indefinite. Recently, affected by the market, the shipping industry has declined even further than before. Therefore, they have repeatedly reiterated their previous request to save themselves from impending demise. The Ministry of Finance has consistently responded that the funds cannot be transferred and it is inconvenient to discuss the issuance at this time. However, as far as shipping merchants know, the surplus tonnage surcharge amounts to hundreds of thousands of yuan per year, which would be more than enough to allocate to the fund. Moreover, it would be particularly appropriate to use the money paid by shipping merchants to provide relief to the shipping industry. According to the governments of various countries, they all vigorously maintain the private shipping industry. Even in neighboring Japan, there is a protection policy of reducing ship taxes for ships operating on regular schedules. For the creation of new ships, there is a subsidy of one-quarter of the cost, and the remaining three-quarters can be borrowed at low interest rates. And recently, it has been stipulated that for old ships replaced with new ships, each ton of the old ship can be used to subsidize the construction cost of one ton of the new ship, excluding subsidies for insurance and interest. If we extend this to Europe and America, the United Kingdom has subsidies to maintain irregular ships, amounting to 2 million pounds per year, and new ship subsidies amounting to 10 million pounds per year, as well as relief in the form of exempting ship inspection fees and other procedures. Germany has 20 million marks per year specifically for maintaining the shipping industry. France has 500 million francs in long-term low-interest loans. Italy has 300 million lira in annual subsidies. The United States allocates 200 million US dollars per year to private shipping merchants, specifically for their use, with an annual interest rate of only 3%. Shipping merchants are even requesting an annual interest rate of only 0.5%. And recently, President Roosevelt requested Congress to allocate 30 million US dollars annually to subsidize the shipping industry. Other countries such as Norway, Finland, Portugal, and Spain all have rewards or subsidies, valuing and favoring them in every possible way. No wonder they are flourishing and developing day by day. Although our country's Provisional Constitution has articles on rewarding and protecting the private shipping industry, there are no actual benefits. In addition, the financial community does not accept ship mortgages. Moreover, at this critical time of survival, the government has consistently refused to issue the shipping industry public bonds that have been approved. This lifeline that shipping merchants have been relying on the government to provide for urgent relief has been declared hopeless. This is the fifth difficulty.

Private Shipping on the Verge of Extinction: Hoping for Your Accomplishment

The circumstances of shipping merchants have the above-mentioned difficulties, coupled with the fact that current business is increasingly declining. The current situation is difficult to sustain, and is truly in dire straits. If we continue to sit idly by without taking action, the private shipping industry will inevitably collapse beyond recovery. Our association, as a shipping merchant organization, has accurate information and feels it is difficult to remain silent. However, repeated requests to the government have been unsuccessful. Pacing back and forth, we are unable to devise a plan. Now, due to overwhelming worry, we have no choice but to appeal to your esteemed committee, earnestly begging for assistance so that the dying private shipping industry can have a chance of revival. We hope for your accomplishment, which will not only be appreciated by shipping merchants. Therefore, we respectfully submit this document, hoping that you will review it, approve its implementation, and await your orders with utmost trepidation. Respectfully submitted to the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, Yu Hede, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association.

Records of Contemporary Figures' Whereabouts

Wu Tiecheng took the night train out of Beijing last night and arrived in Shanghai at 7:15 this morning. Chen Diaoyuan and Yuan Liang took the night train to Beijing yesterday. Wu Zhihui and Miao Bin took the express train out of Beijing yesterday morning and arrived in Shanghai at 2:30 in the afternoon.

Additional Points Following the Report of the Telephone Expert Committee

Discussing the Extent of Increase in Business and Residential Telephone Charges If the Metered Billing Method is to be Continued

The addendum to the report on the telephone problem by the Special Committee of Telephone Experts of the Public Works Department has now been submitted. Yesterday, it was discussed by the Public Utilities Committee of the Public Works Department. When the experts submitted the addendum to the board, they stated that during the meeting of the Public Utilities Committee on the 28th of last month, they had been asked to respond to the matters inquired about in Section 3 of the terms of reference for investigating telephone matters. This has now been done. As for the reason why it was not answered in the general report before, it has been explained on the first page of the general report. The original text of the addendum is translated and recorded below. Section 3 of the terms of reference states: If the metered billing method is maintained, then (1) business telephones, (2) residential telephones, and (3) other items should each increase by how much. The method by which the metered billing rate schedule is gradually obtained is the same as that detailed on page 15 of the general report (Public Bulletin 622 and 623). According to the above-mentioned record, the net profit of the company's operating capital may fall to 8.62% by the end of this year. Furthermore, by the end of this year, the total number of telephones may decrease by 400. Therefore, the company's revenue and expenditure on these telephone rental fees next year will inevitably be lower than this year. In addition, since the expenditure on investment has increased this year, the depreciation that should be accrued from January 1 next year will also slightly increase (Public Bulletin 614, paragraph 2). Now, in order to determine the price of the metered billing method that can offset the monthly fees of 11 yuan and 7 yuan stated in the report, business telephones must pay 15.5 yuan per month, and residential telephones must pay 9.25 yuan per month. And users who currently pay per call should henceforth be charged 11 yuan per month for 150 calls. The surcharge for desk phones should increase to 1.5 yuan, and the fee for extensions should increase to 2 yuan. In the general report, we have discussed in detail the reasons why the metered billing method is not suitable for Shanghai. We firmly believe that if this method continues to be implemented, the number of telephones will inevitably decrease day by day. And as far as we know, many smaller users are anticipating that the per-call billing method will be implemented in the future, and have not yet canceled their telephones. However, if the per-call billing method ceases to be implemented, they will probably also stop using their telephones. Our previous advocacy for the per-call billing method was not only to retain existing users, but also to attract new users in the future, because small users feel that the new prices are lower than the old ones. Therefore, when responding to the request to draft a metered billing price schedule, all we can say is that we not only do not advocate the use of the metered billing method, but on the contrary, we must resolutely criticize its flaws.

Telecommunications Government Bonds Collateral Loan Successful

Totaling Six Million Yuan, Various Banks Undertake to Borrow Separately: Section Chief Zhou Carries the Loan Agreement Back to Beijing for Approval and Signature

The Ministry of Transportation's telecommunications government bonds, worth 10 million yuan, have been in contact with Shanghai banking circles to mortgage a loan of 6 million yuan. Since the positive and negative directors of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Shen Shuyu and Zhou Shouliang, and the Ministry of Transportation's representative, Zhou Wenduan, section chief of the Telecommunications Department, have been actively proceeding, a successful agreement has already been reached. The total amount is 6 million yuan, which is undertaken by banks such as the Central Bank. The interest rate is 8%, and it is planned to be paid off in one year. International telephone fee revenue is used as the guarantee. The loan agreement has already been agreed upon. Zhou Wenduan, section chief of the Ministry of Transportation, took the night express train to Beijing last night to request instructions from the Ministry of Transportation and report on the progress. After the Minister of Transportation, Zhu Jia-hua, first signs and affixes his seal, he will then take it to Shanghai and send it to each bank for signature, and then the loan can be disbursed. The amount undertaken by each bank is roughly allocated as follows: the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications jointly acknowledge 3.1 million yuan; the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, 1.2 million yuan; Shanghai, 300,000 yuan; the Continental Bank, the Jin Cheng Bank, the Zhongnan Bank, and the Yanyeh Bank jointly acknowledge 800,000 yuan; Zhejiang Industrial Bank and Kenye Bank each acknowledge 150,000 yuan; Guohuo Bank and Siming Bank each acknowledge 100,000 yuan; Shiye Bank and Guohua Bank each acknowledge 50,000 yuan; totaling 6 million yuan.

Various Trade Associations Submit to the Fifth Plenary Session: Clearly Order a Reduction in Rent

Representatives of the Rent Reduction Association Decide to Go to Beijing to Petition

Dagong News Agency reports that over forty trade associations in this city, including the salted fish industry, have submitted a joint petition to the Fifth Plenary Session, requesting that the relevant authorities be instructed to clearly define rent reduction standards. At the same time, the Municipal Rent Reduction Committee has decided to send representatives to Beijing to petition. Yesterday, a meeting of the petition delegation was convened to discuss petition procedures. Details are recorded below.

Submissions from Various Industries: Over forty trade associations, including the salted fish industry and the sauce and wine industry, jointly submitted a document to the Fifth Plenary Session yesterday, stating: "The submission is for requesting a prompt and clear definition of rent reduction in order to alleviate the people's difficulties and eliminate disputes. We believe that our country's economic decline has reached its extreme point. The rural economy has already fallen into bankruptcy, and the urban commercial sector is also declining daily. Even just looking at the corner of Shanghai, business is sluggish, far from what it once was. There are many unemployed, and it is difficult to provide employment. Purchasing power is weak, and price indices are therefore gradually decreasing. However, only the rent item remains at the level of five or six years ago, with no hope of reducing the burden. Is this not a kind of abnormal phenomenon? Food, clothing, housing, and transportation are the four necessities of life. At this time of chaos, famine, and increasingly severe recession, in order to maintain life, one can indeed reduce clothing and food, and walk instead of taking transportation, to strive for self-help. However, only the rent for housing, because the power is in the hands of the owners, is a particularly heavy burden that cannot be resolved. It is still impossible to adapt to the environment and slightly alleviate the difficulty. Those owners are people who own assets, and their lives are certainly better than those of ordinary tenants. If they could slightly reduce the rent, it would certainly not harm them in the slightest, while the tenants would have benefited greatly. However, in recent years, despite the appeals and requests of tenants, there are very few who have considered the overall situation and granted rent reductions. Therefore, looking around, all that can be seen is a sluggish market, rows of empty houses, and several businesses forced to close every day. Those who have been sued for rent arrears and ruined their families are countless. If we do not urgently seek to save the future of society, we do not know where it will end. Fortunately, the Plenary Session has opened in Beijing, and representatives from the entire party are gathered together. They should have detailed discussions on national and people's livelihoods. Especially Shanghai, as the commercial center of the country, should strive to make it prosperous. In addition to the representatives sent by the Shanghai Municipal Rent Reduction Committee to petition, we humbly submit the following details, begging for your review. We earnestly request that you consider the decline of Shanghai's commercial sector and the crisis of the social economy, and promptly and decisively issue a clear order to reduce rent in order to alleviate the difficulties of the entire Shanghai population. We cannot express our eagerness and anticipation enough. Respectfully submitted to the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party."

Decisions of the Rent Reduction Association: The Shanghai Municipal Rent Reduction Committee's Beijing petition delegation held a public temporary meeting in the association hall at 3:00 PM yesterday to discuss matters related to the Beijing petition. Nine people, including Li Aokui, Wang Hesong, Ge Futian, Chen Jiufeng, Wang Jingdong, and Jin Chuxiang, attended. Li Aokui was publicly elected as chairman. The chairman first reported, and then the matters for discussion were discussed. (1) The proposal to schedule a petition to Beijing was resolved. It was decided that the petition would be held in Beijing on the morning of the 11th of this month, gathering at the North Station to take the express train. (2) The proposal to select a drafter for the Beijing petition submission was resolved. It was decided that Ge Futian would be responsible for drafting, with the following content: (1) Requesting a clear order to reduce rent by 40%. (2) Once the market recovers, the original state will be restored. (3) The funds obtained from the rent reduction in the first two months will be used to help disaster relief. (4) After three months, the tenants will enjoy the benefits. (5) It is stipulated that the interest on real estate leases must not exceed 5%.

In recent years, the Dutch East Indies has restricted the import of 58 kinds of foreign goods, which is beneficial to our country, because if genuine Chinese goods are imported into the Dutch East Indies, there will be no obstacles. As for the economic situation of overseas Chinese, although it has improved slightly recently, it has still not been able to get rid of the impact of the recession. This situation is the same in all parts of Nanyang, not only in the Dutch East Indies. What overseas Chinese feel most painful about is the local government's levy of business income tax. According to the regulations of the Dutch government, the business income tax is levied at 45%. At a time when the world economy is in recession, overseas Chinese are really unable to bear this heavy burden.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs Request to Abolish the Collection of Pig Tax at the Gaoka Checkpoint in Jiangbei

Taxing Goods as the Object is Actually Repeating the Mistakes of the Former Likin System

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying, "To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the sixth of this month, we received a letter from the Fresh Pig Vending Trade Association, stating that the pig merchants Zhang Yiyuan, Xue Dawu, etc., from Dongtai wrote, 'Since we merchants suffered from the disturbance of the communist bandits, and then added frequent water interest, rural bankruptcy, and those who maintain a line of livelihood rely entirely on the pigs produced in Dongtai, which are transported to Shanghai for sale. We scrape for meager profits to avoid hunger for several family members. After Jiangbei Special Tax sent Chang to collect business tax on transporting pigs, we merchants tried our best to bear the burden and abide by the rules. Unexpectedly, this spring, the Dongtai Business Tax Bureau had a whimsical idea and privately set up checkpoints, intercepting our pig boats along the way and coercing us to collect pig tax again. If one pig pays one tax and passes through the special tax collection office, the ticket should be verified and released. However, the special tax collection office not only does not verify and release, but also needs to count the number and report the payment, which means one pig pays two taxes, and the people's strength is really unimaginable. It is found that the Dongtai Business Tax Bureau privately uses the Tai Dong Business Tax ticket to collect business tax on transporting pigs. The ticket is written in blue ink, and there are words on the ticket specifically for cattle tax. Since it is a cattle tax ticket, how can it be used for pig transport tax? This is a certain and unchangeable principle. It also uses a note to collect pig tax. Inspecting the stamp on the ticket is a long strip shape. This kind of shady scene, layer by layer of malpractices, is known to those who do not need to be enlightened. We merchants are at a time when we are forced by livelihood and it is difficult to bear this one pig and two taxes. We especially present the facts with tears, and ask your association to examine and approve, and to take pity on the merchants' difficulties, and to allow us to transfer the facts to the authorities and strictly order the Dongtai Business Tax Bureau to stop collecting the tax and punish the director of the bureau, Chen Yunzhang, in accordance with the law, in order to rectify the law and discipline and pay attention to the people's livelihood. (Omission) The business tax is a behavior tax, so the same business entity and the same business behavior must not be taxed repeatedly. The tax should be collected at the business location and should not be collected at the passing place. This is the fundamental difference between the business tax and the likin. It is now found that the attached photographic receipt shows that the bureau did not collect taxes on a monthly basis in accordance with the short-term business regulations. It is true that the tax is collected once every time the goods pass. It is obvious that it is a likin checkpoint. Furthermore, the Zhang Yiyuan company paid the tax in Dongtai on August 29th, and the next day, August 30th, the tax was collected again in Rugao, where the ship passed. It is even more obvious that checkpoints are set up along the way to intercept, and the business entity is not the object of taxation, but the goods are the object of taxation. Recently, merchants have complained about the business tax, saying that the tax has not been implemented for a long time, and it has already followed the mistakes of the former likin system. Other places are not mentioned for the time being. Jiangsu Province is close to the capital, and the national government orders should be implemented without hindrance. The illegal handling of the pig business tax has been telegraphed to your ministry by the association, and a case has been filed for strict correction. After several months, the order is still being played with. Where is the national code of conduct? It is appropriate to re-attach the photographic receipt and telegraph it to your ministry for verification. We hope that you will strictly investigate and correct it, and must abolish the checkpoints along the way and dismiss and punish the contractors. How can we express our public gratitude? Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows."

On the 28th of last month, the Japanese-language Shanghai Daily published an interview with Mr. Lin, a professor of bookkeeping at the Tongwen Academy of this port, who criticized the report of the Public Works Department Telephone Expert Committee. Yesterday, the four national experts of the Expert Committee sent an official letter to the newspaper to respond to Mr. Lin's opinions. The main points of the expert's official letter are excerpted as follows: "We were very pleased to read Mr. Lin's great argument the other day. However, since Mr. Lin is dissatisfied with our report, we also have considerable regrets about what Mr. Lin said. There are several words in Mr. Lin's thesis that have greatly alarmed us, which can be briefly stated. It seems to say that "the numbers are not credible and can be arbitrarily increased or decreased to distort any facts," etc. We do not want to be too demanding on Mr. Lin, but it is strange that what Mr. Lin said was actually said by a bookkeeping professor, because the first duty of a bookkeeper is to audit the accuracy of the numbers and represent concrete and unchangeable facts. Furthermore, we especially want to share with people that we have stated one by one the matters within the scope of our authority, but Mr. Lin claimed in the interview that the public's position should not be ignored in the report, etc. In fact, when we were drafting the report, we not only did not ignore this point, but also exceeded the scope of our authority in fact. However, the matters that we were ordered to investigate must first be answered one by one before we can involve other points. Taking the first point that we should answer as an example, the question is "Does the telephone company have the right to increase prices?" After investigating, we found that the company does have the right to increase prices if the profits are insufficient after fulfilling certain conditions. According to the express provisions of the franchise contract, it should have the right to increase prices. As for other issues, such as whether the interest rate is appropriate, whether the public can afford it, etc., are indeed not within the scope of our authority and there is no way to add any opinions. Moreover, the franchise contract clearly stipulates that the interest rate on operating investment should be percentage plus percentage two, and also specifies what is operating capital, so we have no way to criticize the company's fundraising methods. As for items such as income tax and management fees, we did not comment on them because we were ordered not to discuss them. Furthermore, as for the land price, what we relied on was a certificate from the land price estimator at the time, and the valuation had been approved by the Public Works Department of the Public Works Bureau. Of course, the evaluation of land price cannot be as accurate a science as bookkeeping. At most, it can only accept the opinions of signed experts, which is also what we have already done. We are very grateful to Mr. Lin for explaining the complicated procedures in the report, but we feel that there is no need to add any further in-depth discussion other than this reply."

Discovery of Three Kidnapping Cases on the Mingsheng Steamer

Kidnapped Women Severely Abused; Perpetrators Awaiting Court Interrogation

On the morning of the day before yesterday, around 10 a.m., Customs and Water Police, upon orders, dispatched Huang Zhencun, Wang Haiquan, and Xu Jueul, together with Chen Shaoting, an investigator from the Chinese Women and Children Relief Association, to inspect the Mingsheng steamer of the Yihe Company's Northern Seas route. They successfully uncovered three kidnapping cases in the steerage section. Liu Xiangsheng and Zhong Wanshi were found to have jointly kidnapped a thirteen-year-old girl from Yangzhou, Liu Xiaolianzi. Hu Wangshi was found to have lured and kidnapped a twelve-year-old girl from Danyang, Lin Xiuying. Su Bao was found to have kidnapped Xu Zhangshi (19 years old), a young married woman from Changzhou. All were intended to be sold in Qingdao. They were immediately taken to the police station for separate interrogations. According to the first case, the defendant Liu Shengxiang confessed: "I am thirty-nine years old, from Anhui. Zhong Wanshi lured Liu Xiaolianzi from the street to her home. Jiang Guifang, who lives with her, planned to sell her to Qingdao. Last night, after Wanshi and I escorted Liu Xiaolianzi onto the ship, I tricked her into an empty room and raped her; this is true." Wanshi's confession was similar to Liu Xiangsheng's. According to the kidnapped Liu Xiaolianzi, "Since I was a child, I was raised as a child bride in the home of a certain family in the Sun Temple of Zhabei. Because I was abused by my parents-in-law, I escaped once last year and was sent to the Qiliang Shelter, where I stayed for over a year before my parents-in-law took me back. Now, my parents-in-law have resumed their old habits, beating me so badly that I urinate blood. Unable to bear the pain, I took another opportunity to escape and met the defendants, who offered to arrange a marriage for me as a child bride in Qingdao. I didn't know I was being deceived. I bled a lot during the rape," and so on. According to the second case, the defendant Hu Wangshi confessed: "I am thirty years old, from Suzhou. The girl I brought, Lin Xiuying, was bought by my husband's friend, Wang Jiesan, in Danyang from her parents for 120 yuan. He sent her to my home ten days ago to stay for a few days. On the morning of the fifth of this month, he told me to send her to a small inn on Avenue Joffre. In the afternoon, three people from Shandong, Wang Jinsheng and Cao Zurong, and Zhang Bingxiao from Changzhou, claimed to have come to Shanghai from Qingdao and planned to take Xiuying to Qingdao for marriage. They told me to send her to Qingdao, falsely claiming that she was born when I was eighteen, and promising to reward me with ten yuan after the matter was completed. That night, at 9 p.m., Wang Jiesan, Wang Jinsheng, and Cao Zurong brought Lin Xiuying to the Mingsheng steamer. Wang Jiesan returned first. When inspectors arrived, Wang and Cao also took the opportunity to escape," and so on. The kidnapped Xiuying also said that her parents had arranged to sell her to someone else. According to the third case, the defendant Cao Subao confessed: "I am thirty-one years old, from Changzhou, and live near the Public University Yarn Factory in Yangshupu. I know the female worker Xu Zhangshi. I conspired with my friend Jin Liugen to kidnap Zhangshi and sell her to Qingdao. We were caught on the ship," and so on. According to the kidnapped Xu Zhangshi, also known as Sanmei: "I work at the Public University No. 1 Yarn Factory. I met a female coworker named Xiaomei a month ago. Half a month ago, Xiaomei introduced me to her husband, Cao Subao. Xiaomei said that the wages in Shanghai were low and the wages in the Qingdao factory were high, and that she would like to go to Qingdao with me to work. On the afternoon of the 31st of last month, at 6 p.m., I received four yuan in wages. When I left the factory, I saw Cao Subao and his friend Jin Liugen already waiting. They said that the ship to Qingdao had already arrived in Shanghai. Jin accompanied me by car to a small inn to stay. That night, Jin raped me once. The next day, Cao also came to the inn. Jin then excused himself and left. Cao raped me again. By the 5th of this month, Cao had raped me three times, and Jin raped me every night. Unable to bear the pain, on the morning of the 6th, Cao accompanied me onto the ship. Jin said he would come in four days, but suddenly we were arrested," and so on. After the detectives obtained their confessions separately, they ordered the kidnapped women to be temporarily sent to the Relief Association for care, and the defendants were all detained. They also ordered the original detectives to strictly arrest the accomplices. Yesterday afternoon, they ordered detectives from the Putuo Road Police Station to arrest Jin Liugen, an accomplice of Cao Subao, and bring him back for joint trial. The three kidnapping cases will be transferred to the District Court for trial today.

Hu Wenhu and Others Initiate the Establishment of the New Yongding Construction Association

Hu Wenhu Elected President, Lin Luming General Manager; General Association Established in Shanghai, Branch Associations Established in Nanyang and Other Places

Shanghai News reports that Hu Wenhu, Lin Luming, Hu Guigeng, Su Lezhen, and others, in view of the fact that their hometown of Yongding County in Fujian Province has suffered from banditry for years, houses have been burned, fields have been deserted, and the economy has been depleted, initiated the organization of the New Yongding Construction Association to strive for a hometown rescue movement. The inaugural meeting was held yesterday morning at 9 a.m. on the ninth floor of the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge. More than eighty people attended. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Mao Yun, and the Social Affairs Bureau, Rao Qiangsheng, attended to provide guidance. Details are as follows:

Chairman's Report: Chairman Lin Luming, master of ceremonies Li Guangteng, performed the formalities. First, the chairman reported on the preparations, stating that today's inaugural meeting of the New Yongding Construction Association would briefly report on the motivation for the establishment of the association and future plans. Yongding was a good paradise twenty years ago. In the past twenty years, banditry has been continuous, and people have been unable to make a living, causing many fellow villagers to be homeless or unable to return home. Whenever they gather and talk about it, they feel extremely painful. Therefore, we initiated the organization of the New Yongding Construction Association to restore past prosperity. We rely on the efforts of the people themselves and the assistance of the government to build a new Yongding, which will surely be twice as effective with half the effort. We hope that everyone will unite together and use a spirit of sacrifice to carry out the hometown rescue movement, without fear of difficulties, without complacency, and without selfishness. Only then will the future be bright.

Matters for Discussion: Representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Mao Yun, and the Social Affairs Bureau, Rao Qiangsheng, delivered speeches successively. Hu Guigeng gave a speech. Then, the association's charter was discussed and a general outline of the plan was adopted. The association's general association is located in Shanghai, and branch associations are established in Singapore, Batavia, Yangon, Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, and other places. The New Yongding Construction Three-Year Plan covers six major plans: security, transportation, education, industry and commerce, hygiene, and agriculture and forestry, which are quite comprehensive.

Verification of Self-Rehabilitated Opium Addicts; Twenty-Six Designated Hospitals

Opium Addicts Willing to Pay Fees Should Go to Various Hospitals for Examination as Soon as Possible; Those Unable to Pay Fees Will Be Sent to Drug Rehabilitation Centers for Verification

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau is handling the registration of opium addicts. Previously, the number of opium addicts who applied for self-rehabilitation was very large. It is difficult to determine whether their rehabilitation is genuine. The bureau is deeply concerned that cunning individuals may use the name of self-rehabilitation to secretly smoke opium, which would be a profound malpractice. The bureau has drafted measures and notified all subordinate units that opium addicts who apply for self-rehabilitation must be examined by a hospital designated by the Health Bureau to obtain a certificate and submit a pledge not to smoke opium again, all of which should be submitted to the bureau for record. If they commit opium smoking again, the bureau may send them to a temporary drug rehabilitation center for verification at any time. The bureau had previously requested the Health Bureau to designate various hospitals to undertake this opium cessation examination work. It has now been learned that a reply has been received from the Health Bureau yesterday, designating a total of twenty-six hospitals. Upon receiving the reply, the bureau immediately ordered all sub-bureaus to notify all opium addicts who are voluntarily undergoing rehabilitation that those who are willing to pay fees may go to the Municipal Opium Cessation Hospital and the designated hospitals for examination to obtain a certificate and submit it to the bureau for record. Those who are unable to pay fees will be summoned to the bureau for transfer to the Municipal Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center for verification. It is also heard that in order to facilitate general opium addicts who voluntarily undergo rehabilitation, the bureau intends to send a letter to the Health Bureau requesting that the fees for opium cessation and examination be charged by the designated hospitals at a minimum limit. Zhao Anzhi Opens Painting Exhibition in Beijing

Zhao Anzhi, a painter from Wujin, is from a prominent family in Lanling. In his youth, he was known for his scholarly achievements. In his spare time, he often used the court styles of the Song Dynasty as his model, incorporating the changes of the Ming and Qing Dynasties, and integrating the achievements of various schools. He combined various schools into one, while still creating his own unique style. Whether he paints figures or landscapes, his images are always extraordinary. His meticulous paintings of flowers, birds, grasses, and insects are particularly famous for their gorgeous colors. In the spring of the 18th year, he was specially invited to exhibit his works at the National Art Exhibition, ranking among the best. In the winter of the 19th year, he won a gold medal at the Belgian Centennial Progress World Exposition. In the mid-spring of the 22nd year, he responded to the Chicago Exposition and received great praise from the people of that country. He participated again when it reopened the following year. In the early spring of the 23rd year, he responded to the invitation of the Sino-German Painting Exhibition and toured through England, the Netherlands, Italy, Switzerland, France, and Czechoslovakia. Many of his works were purchased. It is hoped that his fame will rival that of great artists. This is not only the extension of his reputation in painting, but also a major event for our country internationally. Chu Minyi and others, considering that many men of letters have gathered in Beijing recently, specially advised him to display his fine works of the past ten years at the Martyrs' Shrine in the First Park of Nanjing for public exhibition for five days, from the 9th to the 13th of this month. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion.

A Visit to the Rubber Industry—Zhengtai Rubber Factory—

—Lou Lizhai

The rubber industry in our country is not only one of the emerging industries, but also the fastest-growing industry in recent years. The first people in our country to engage in this industry were in Guangzhou. Later, some people in Shanghai also engaged in it, and the speed of development has exceeded that of Guangzhou. In 1919, Shanghai had the Zhonghua Rubber Factory, which manufactured shoe soles. This was the beginning of the rubber industry in Shanghai. However, the factory only operated for one year and then closed down due to losses. After that, the Jiangwan Model Factory and others were established one after another, transitioning from manufacturing shoe soles to making galoshes. They rose up like a storm, reaching their peak for a time. By 1931, it was even more developed. There were 48 rubber factories in the city, with a total capital of approximately 4 million yuan, 12,000 workers, and a total output value of over 10 million yuan. This was the most prosperous era of the Shanghai rubber industry in the past. However, the good times did not last long. The January 28th Shanghai Incident broke out, some factories were destroyed, production capacity declined, and foreign goods took the opportunity to dump their products, seizing the domestic market. After the war, the market was sluggish, sales were slow, and the turnover of working capital was inflexible. As a result, many factories closed down and stopped work one after another. After 1933, it became even more declining, with a tendency to go from bad to worse. By the first half of last year, only a dozen or so were able to maintain operation. By November, because too many factories had closed down, production decreased, and demand exceeded supply. The market gradually became active, so the factories that had stopped work resumed work one after another, and the future seems promising.

At 2 p.m. on September 30th, a group of five of us went to the Zhengtai Rubber Factory to visit the rubber industry. Mr. Yang Shaozhen and Mr. Hong Fumei of the factory warmly received us and first told us about the history of the factory.

The factory was established in 1926, with the factory site on Tangshan Road. It specializes in manufacturing Daxipai galoshes. Later, it was acquired by Panyi Chang Rubber Factory. At that time, the Wannianqing and Sanba brands of galoshes produced by Yichang were still produced by them. As business developed, the Tangshan Road factory was no longer sufficient, so a second factory was added on Dalianwan Road. The original factory on Tangshan Road was called the First Factory. In February 1933, the First Factory was destroyed by an electrical fire, and the loss of assets and inventory reached 200,000 yuan. The business losses are not included, which was truly a catastrophe for the factory. After that, the second factory expanded its scope and made every effort to reorganize. In terms of equipment, it sought safety and stability. In terms of production, because the sales of galoshes had gradually become sluggish at that time, it reduced production and stopped making Wannianqing and Sanba brand galoshes, and increased the production of Huili ball shoes to compete with the imported Redo basketball shoes. Recently, it has increased the production of Wanli shoes. "Wanli" is used to describe the sturdiness of the shoes, emphasizing that they will not break even if worn for ten thousand miles. After such a reorganization after the disaster, the factory is now gradually recovering its former appearance.

After Mr. Yang and Mr. Hong finished talking about the history of the factory, they led us to visit the production process.

The main raw material for galoshes, Huili ball shoes, and Wanli shoes is rubber. Rubber is made from the sap of the rubber tree. Rubber trees grow in the tropics. In our country, only Qiongyai produces it, but the quantity is very small and has not been developed. Therefore, the rubber used by various rubber factories is purchased from overseas. The rubber used by this factory is purchased from Singapore.

The purchased rubber is mixed with white powder mixed with lime, magnesium carbonate, and zinc white, sulfur, and other organic accelerators, and mixed with heat and pressure to make hot rubber. This rubber is divided into thick and thin types. The former is used for making shoe soles, and the latter is used for making shoe uppers.

To make galoshes, you only need to glue the thick and thin rubber to the inside, cut them into shoe soles and uppers, glue the soles and uppers together, and then polish and dry them. As for Huili ball shoes and Wanli shoes, it is more complicated. The inside of the upper must be glued to both sides of the thin rubber separately to make the upper, and the thick rubber must be cut into the sole with an electric knife. Then, the sole and upper are glued together and dried in a steaming room to complete the process. (To be continued)

(Central News Agency, Beiping, 7th) Zhang Xiesheng, a service member of the Boy Scouts of China, traveled on foot through eleven provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Hebei, Shandong, and Anhui. Municipal Education Bureau Orders Issuance of Notice Regarding Purchase of Phonetic Alphabet Copper Molds

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday issued an order to the Printing Trade Association and all printing houses: "I. Regarding the Ministry of Education's instructions, it is imperative that printing companies, bookstores, etc., that print and sell textbooks for elementary schools and public schools directly contact the Shanghai Chung Hwa Book Company for purchase. Therefore, this order includes a copy of the Notice Regarding Purchase of Phonetic Alphabet Copper Molds, which is attached below for compliance."

Notice Regarding Purchase of Phonetic Alphabet Copper Molds:

1. The phonetic alphabet copper molds cast by the Ministry of Education are sold as a set in sizes 2, 3, 4, and 5, and are not sold separately.

2. The actual price of the copper mold for each size is calculated by multiplying the per-character price of each size by the total number of characters; no discounts are offered. The per-character price for each size is as follows: Size 2: 23.5 cents per character; Size 3: 22 cents per character; Size 4: 21 cents per character; Size 5: 20 cents per character.

3. When placing an order, the purchaser must first pay a deposit of 600 national currency units. Subsequently, payment for each size must be made upon completion, and a set will be received. The deposit paid will be deducted when paying for the last set of goods.

4. The order in which goods are received will follow the order of the sizes ordered, i.e., those who ordered earlier will have priority in receiving the goods.

5. Orders can be placed at the Third Section of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Education in Nanjing, the Shanghai Chung Hwa Book Company, and its branches in various locations.

6. After five sets of copper molds have been sold, all sectors may imitate the casting in the same style, and purchasers may cast and sell lead characters. However, imitation products must be examined by the Ministry of Education.

News of Chrysanthemum Exhibitions in Various Places

Yutang People's Education Center: Since the Yutang People's Education Center was changed to provincial administration, and with the active promotion of Niu Tisheng, Huang Meixian, and Niu Changyao, it has shown a sudden and rapid rise. It has achieved practical results in improving agriculture, organizing cooperation, increasing the livelihood of the people, implementing life education, experimenting with the "little teacher" system, and guiding women in household affairs and side businesses. In particular, the implementation of the horticulture-based industry creation is unique in the country. It is learned that the Yutang Education Undertaking Steering Committee Chairman Huang Meixian and Niu Changyao have decided to hold various educational activities on the 9th and 10th of this month to entertain guests. It is also heard that the society has about 20,000 chrysanthemum plants of all kinds on display, collecting rare and valuable varieties from home and abroad, and cultivating strange and superb shapes, such as inverted waterfalls, roaring lions, independent towering plants of several feet, and towering ten-level pagodas, with colorful and magnificent flowers, which are rare to see. It is also heard that the Yutang Women's Household Affairs Research Association has specially set up seats to sell chrysanthemum tea, egg fried rice, and Yutang local products to entertain guests passing by to visit.

Jinan University: The chrysanthemums produced by the National Jinan University in Zhenru have always been famous. Although there has been excessive autumn rain this year, making cultivation difficult, the large potted upright chrysanthemums of the school have hundreds of flowers per pot, plump and fresh, making them the crown of Shanghai. It is now scheduled that on the anniversary of the founding of the school on the 12th of this month, all the famous chrysanthemums will be displayed in the Zhiyuan Hall of the school for the public to view. The school sincerely welcomes all visitors, and it is expected that there will be a grand occasion.

News from the Chung Hwa Correspondence School of Accountancy

The Chung Hwa Correspondence School of Accountancy, located at 275 Gordon Road, Shanghai, was founded by the famous accountant Mr. Shen Liren. After ten years of dedicated operation, its students are located at home and abroad. Some have become practicing accountants, some teach at universities, and some hold important military and political positions, but most are accounting personnel in ordinary industrial and commercial circles. As a result, the total number of trainees and apprentices reaches 3,000, and the school has gained a great reputation in society. The school's textbooks are all personally written by Mr. Shen Liren. It is said that he has spent a long time researching when editing, so its content is very different from other books on the market. Therefore, universities such as Jinan University, Guanghua University, and Chizhi University have all adopted it as a textbook, and various libraries have also purchased it. In order to innovate correspondence education, when lecturing at various universities, he specially sends Chang Jiang to record the lectures of each professor on a daily basis, compile lecture notes, and provide them exclusively for the reading of the school's correspondence students. It is heard that the auditing subject was originally taught by Mr. Shen at Guanghua University, and the notes have now been printed and distributed to the school's correspondence students, so the students in the school's correspondence course are no different from being in the classroom and listening to the teachings in person. The transcription of the other subjects is also being compiled in order, and it is also heard that the school enrolls students all year round and has detailed regulations for the convenience of those interested in studying accounting.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (88)

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Mr. Bhaer didn't approve of it. I didn't tell Mr. Brooke, I ran away myself."

"He knew it too, and naturally felt sorry at the time, but it doesn't matter. You skipped it!" Mrs. Jo asked again when she saw him limping again.

"When I climbed over a wall, a stone fell down and hit my foot, shattering it. I don't care," so he forced himself to endure the pain that each step gave him.

Mrs. Bhaer helped him into his room, and as soon as he entered, he collapsed into a chair, his head resting back, his face pale with exhaustion and pain.

"My poor Don! Drink this cup and eat some food. You're home now, and Mother Bhaer will take good care of you."

Schedule for the Chinese Football Association Cup

To Begin Next Week

The Chinese Football Association Cup, with A, B, and C divisions, has twenty participating teams. The committee has arranged the groups, and the competition is scheduled to begin next week.
