A Division Cup

B Division Cup

C Division Cup

New Football Rules

Disqualification of Players Changed to Awarding a Free Kick

The Chinese National Sports Federation has received official notification from the International Football Association regarding a new rule set for this season, which has been decided to be adopted. The rule is hereby announced as follows:

Add the following sentence after the third sentence of the first paragraph of Article 13: "If the game is stopped due to the discovery of improper behavior by a player, then the game should be continued with a free kick awarded to the player's opposing team." The full text is changed as follows:

First paragraph of Article 13, third sentence: "The referee should warn players who engage in improper behavior during the game." Fourth sentence: "If the game is stopped due to the discovery of improper behavior by a player, then the game should be continued with a free kick awarded to the player's opposing team." The fifth sentence and subsequent sentences remain the same.

Under the old rules, the referee used a throw-in to start the game in the above situation. Now, a penalty kick is awarded, giving the offending party's opponent an advantage, which is a proper penalty.

Opening Date of Xiqing Basketball Tournament Changed to Later Date

—Scheduled for December 2nd

C Division Cancelled This Year, A and B Divisions Remain the Same; Participants Must Purchase Tickets for 50 Yuan

This year's Xiqing Basketball Tournament will still be held as usual, with only minor changes. The opening date is later than in previous years and has been scheduled for December 2nd, after Christmas and New Year's. The number of teams invited to participate is also less than in previous years. It is expected that the tournament must be completed before January 25th. Invitation letters have been sent out, about fifty in total. The C division has been cancelled this year. The A division will accommodate about ten teams, and the B division will accommodate sixteen teams. The B division will still be divided into two sections, using a single-round robin system. The top teams in B division 1 and 2 will then compete in a final. Registration will close on November 5th. In order to subsidize expenses, each participating team must purchase tickets for 50 yuan, either long-term passes or regular tickets. The participation deposit has been reduced from 25 yuan to 10 yuan.

Malaysian-Chinese Athletes Return South with Honors; Departed Shanghai This Morning

Representatives from All Sectors Went to See Them Off Last Night; General Secretary Lin Wumin Spoke About His Impressions of This Trip

A group of over 150 Malaysian-Chinese athletes and inspection team members, led by the overseas Chinese magnate Mr. Hu Wenhu, came to Shanghai to participate in this year's National Games and achieved excellent results, attracting the attention of the Chinese people. They have now boarded the Italian postal ship Conte Rosso, led by General Secretary Lin Aimin, to return to Singapore. Many people from all sectors went to see them off. Two female athletes will remain in Shanghai to study at Liangjiang. Details are noted as follows:

Participated in the National Games with Remarkable Results

Over one hundred Malaysian-Chinese athletes and inspection team members, led by Mr. Hu Wenhu, came to Shanghai on the 5th of last month to participate in this year's National Games. The results in various sports were quite remarkable, and the football team was particularly strong, earning the praise of the Chinese people. After the closing ceremony of the National Games, apart from team leader Hu Wenhu and the football players who had already returned south, the rest remained in Shanghai and, led by General Secretary Lin Aimin, went to Beijing and Hangzhou for sightseeing. They returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday.

Boarded Ship Last Night, Departed This Morning

The entire team of athletes, led by Lin Aimin, boarded the Italian postal ship Conte Rosso last night to return to Singapore. The ship set sail at 6:00 AM this morning. Those who went to the Zhaoshang North Wharf last night to see them off included Mr. Lan Shiqin, Director of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau of this city, Mr. Hu Guigeng, Shanghai Manager of Tiger Balm, Mr. Li Dachao, representative of the Municipal Government, and dozens of representatives from various organizations. The atmosphere was very enthusiastic. Two female athletes will remain in Shanghai to study at Liangjiang Women's Physical Education College.

General Secretary Lin Delivered a Speech

According to Mr. Lin Aimin, the team's general secretary, he was very pleased to have led the Malaysian-Chinese athletes back to China to participate in the National Games. Apart from the football team, which had already returned to Singapore, the rest all took the ship south tonight (i.e., last night). Among the more than one hundred Malaysian-Chinese athletes and inspection team members, one-third had never returned to China. During their stay of more than a month, they felt extremely excited about the rapid progress of the motherland's construction and the development of all undertakings, and they were particularly grateful for the warm reception from all sectors. He hoped to be able to participate in the next National Games.

Diao Zuoqian Returned to Singapore on the Same Ship

Consul General Diao Zuoqian, who was stationed in Singapore, returned to China at the same time as the Malaysian-Chinese team last month. After staying in Shanghai, he also returned to Singapore on the same ship as the Malaysian-Chinese team last night. According to Diao, in recent years, sports in Southeast Asia have made great progress due to Mr. Hu Wenhu's vigorous promotion. He was satisfied with the performance at the National Games. After returning to Singapore, the promotion of sports among overseas Chinese should be further promoted to make it more widespread.

Fudan University Held a Tea Party to Bid Farewell

The Fudan University Overseas Chinese Student Association specially held a farewell meeting for the Malaysian-Chinese athletes yesterday. More than 60 people attended, including President Li and the Malaysian-Chinese athletes, making it a grand occasion. The meeting began with an introduction by Chairman Yang Wei, followed by speeches by President Li and Secretary-General Jin. Finally, the athlete representatives gave a reply. After the tea party, students Fang Jiazhen and Yan Xingkun led them to visit various departments. The athletes praised the school's various facilities and the spirit of cooperation between teachers and students. In order to warmly entertain the athletes, the school held a garden party to entertain the athletes, performing Peking opera and foreign songs, both Chinese and Western. The meeting ended at around 8:00 PM.

Commercial News

New Gold Transactions in the Financial Market Virtually Nonexistent; Settling Trades Adorn the Gold Market

Only 10,000 Shares; Hovering Around Settlement Prices; Final Small Decline of Eight Jiao

The gold market was even quieter yesterday, with limited trading in the arena. However, major players continued to settle long and short positions, barely adorning the market. Prices hovered around the settlement price of 3 yuan, with an even greater sense of desolation. Upon initial morning inspection, the overseas silver market showed a rise in British silver and stable American silver. Major dealers claimed that after closing, a few speculators bought forward contracts at 0.0625 above the closing price. Forward silver prices in Montreux rose by 5 to 6.5 li. Exchange rates slightly contracted. London raw gold feared one penny. Reports indicated that banks in Hong Kong had stopped paying out coins, with rumors of the government taking the same action as China, but public sentiment remained stable. Outside-market provisional trading opened at 52.3 yuan. Yongli advanced slightly, while Fuxing, Yongheng, Yuyeqing, and Yongze came to sell. Yongli advanced again and retreated, gradually falling below 50 yuan. The morning opening was slightly lower and delayed, waiting for the Central Bank to post its rates. The Central Bank's rates were announced, with British and American rates unchanged. Customs Gold Unit rose by 5 li. The standard gold price was listed at 1149.6 yuan. Sentiment remained stable, and prices rose slightly after the opening. However, due to selling by Tongtai Chang, prices soon retreated back below 50 yuan. Short-sellers Yuanchang and Yong took advantage of the opportunity to buy in, maintaining stability. However, with Tongtai Chang and others periodically releasing shares, the market price hovered around 50 yuan. Major players observed from the sidelines. HSBC's rates and the silver equalization tax remained unchanged. The situation within the arena was idle, with little to no price movement for quite some time. Helplessly, long positions were sold off, and the exchange market slightly eased. Although news from the Hong Kong market was good, sentiment in this city was unaffected. The arena lacked support. Predictions of an increase in Indian silver by 10 annas led to a decline, and the news was weak. Major players maintained positions at low prices. The noon market remained flat, and the after-market opening was also flat. Buying interest was reviving, gradually pulling prices up. The middle portion was extremely stagnant, with short positions slightly covering. Finally, prices broke out of the 50 yuan range, but major long-position holders sold again, preventing the rise. Indian silver did not arrive, making market changes even more difficult. Prices hovered to the end. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

Auxiliary Coins Traded at Twelve Jiao on the Black Market

Since the implementation of the legal tender system, the market price of auxiliary coins has been discussed by Minister Kong, who stipulated a uniform market price to avoid confusing the market situation. Therefore, since the 4th, it has been repeatedly stipulated that each 12 jiao of silver coins is equivalent to 1 yuan, and each 3,000 copper coins is equivalent to 1 yuan. Unexpectedly, small money shops have recently been heavily involved in black market trading, opening up boards and making deals in the market at prices that deviate from the fixed market price of 12 jiao. The price decreased by 0.01 the day before yesterday to 11.9 jiao, and increased by 0.02 yesterday morning to 12.1 jiao. It decreased by 0.006 in the afternoon to 12.004 jiao. The industry leaders in the money business believe that the small money shops are not members of the same industry association, so they are not concerned and ignore the issue. However, if this continues, it is bound to disrupt the market situation of auxiliary coin manipulation.

Since the Ministry of Finance announced the revised legal tender issue, the markets in various industries have been trending towards stability. All were bought by this street.

Yesterday, the tea market for foreign firms was slightly quiet. European firms were still in high demand for high-quality Zhenmei and Mazhu green teas due to active overseas routes. However, the inventory of each tea warehouse was exhausted, and there were no goods available for the market. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson, Concordia, China Tea, and Yongxing foreign firms purchased a total of more than 500 boxes of Zhenmei, Mei Shrimp Eyes, Xi, and Qimen black tea. The market was generally stable.

Sugar Market Sugar Sales Decline, Brown Sugar Slightly Soft

Yesterday's sugar market trend remained flat. The guild's market price for 25 coarse sand white spot was 22 yuan, and transit goods were 6.9 yuan, but no transactions were made. Zhenji No. 1 refined white sugar from this factory was 21.2 yuan, and Nos. 2, 3, 4, and 5 were sold according to rebates. Dong Chi and Dong Bai were both quoted at the original price without success. However, the price of transit goods slightly decreased. YT mark was 6.75 yuan, and URP mark was 6.45 yuan, with some transactions. Only over 100 bags of domestic Chaoqing were released, Gao Huanggang Qing at 11.8 yuan. The other Diao Qing, etc., were still in negotiations and have not yet been released.

North-South Goods Honey Dates Turn Upward Due to Low Inventory

Although honey dates have recently experienced a slow sales period, there are not many inventories in the market. Owners are guarding their goods and selling less, so market prices have rebounded. Yesterday, the market price was 28 yuan for Zheng Gong Tutu Xing, and 24 yuan for Lanxi goods. Upper and lower grades were routinely rebated. The trend is stable.

Metals, Door Number 5 and 6 White Lead Sheets Are in Great Shortage

No. 5 and 6 white lead sheets are essential for battery factories. Since overseas prices have soared, local peers have rushed to hoard and speculate. However, battery factories are actively purchasing, so the circulating goods are in danger of being exhausted. The price per barrel has increased from 28 yuan to 30 yuan, and recently opened at 32 yuan. However, there is a large shortage of inventory, so the public demands 34 yuan to sell. It is reported that Yaohua and Huiming and other battery factories reluctantly made transactions yesterday, selling 15 or 16 barrels at a price of 34 yuan.

In addition, No. 2 and 3 opened at 30 yuan, No. 4 at 29.75 yuan, and No. 7 and above at 32.2 yuan, but the trading volume is not as active as No. 5 and 6.

Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Evening in Sha Wan

— Leng Mo

I hadn't expected to stay in Hong Kong. The forced stay made me stubbornly irritated. Although I had just come out of a village of fewer than ten houses and should have been quite used to solitude, I couldn't deceive my loneliness with quietude in a city with hundreds of thousands of residents. Seeing people on the road greeting each other, or even just exchanging a smile without greeting, I felt a bit jealous. I often went out for walks but would dejectedly run back, only to run out again soon after, always hoping to run into someone I knew and act out the comedy of meeting an old friend in a foreign land. This expectation was somewhat possible. When passing through Wuzhou, I had heard that someone had gone to Hong Kong, and someone else would be going soon. Because I wasn't very familiar with these people, I didn't pay much attention during the hurried passage. Now, I couldn't help but regret it. Actually, even if I had paid attention at the time and made a special visit according to the address, it would have been quite abrupt. I still hoped to run into them on the road and be able to casually greet them. Even if they saw me and greeted me faintly, I would still have to return to my solitude. So, while I eagerly wanted to meet an acquaintance, I was also worried, hoping that the reality would destroy my hope.

Taking the ferry to pass the time had become a habit in my daily life. The four-cent fare carried me on a forty- or fifty-minute voyage, and it could restore the fatigue after wandering for a long time, allowing me to start a new wandering on the other side. During my stay in Hong Kong, I spent much more time in Kowloon on the opposite shore than in Hong Kong. Kowloon's orderly roads were easier to recognize than Hong Kong, and there were no surging crowds. Sometimes, it was even deserted and more suitable for my state of mind at the time. I don't know how many times I had walked along Nathan Road and Prince Edward Road. Because I always came by ferry from Sham Shui Po, I would walk along these two roads to Kowloon City and take the ferry back. If I came by ferry from Kowloon City, I would reverse the route. Ferry rides and walking often took up an entire afternoon. Once, I landed at Kowloon City and, because I went to play at Sung Wong Toi, I lingered for a long time. Afraid that it would be too late to walk to Sham Shui Po, I took a tram. This way, I arrived slightly earlier than usual. Unwilling to return to Hong Kong just yet, I watched people fishing with nets at the pier. These fishermen were selling their catch at any time. The method was also very peculiar. Because every net was sure to catch something, they set the price of each net of fish at one cent, regardless of the quantity. Whoever paid first got the fish that came up in that net. In this way, buyers could try their luck for that one cent. I could say that I was lured by the gambling spirit and also spent one cent. And I was actually very lucky, getting an unprecedented amount. So, I was envied and talked about by other buyers. This made me feel that I could be considered not an unfamiliar person among them.

But this sudden sense of belonging gradually embarrassed me. I had now taken my luck and walked away, but I had no way to deal with this pile of small fish. I didn't have anything to carry them in. So, someone gave me a newspaper. But where could I carry them wrapped in a newspaper? So, I continued to stare blankly at the small fish, holding the newspaper. In this way, my actions at this time became more of a center of attention than the fish in the fisherman's net. I felt that the people around me were gradually increasing, or perhaps even those outside the circle felt that something strange had happened inside the circle. I really hoped that these fish caught from the sea could return to the sea. But I realized that pushing them back would attract even more attention. So, I was forced to accept this luck. Luckily, I ran into an acquaintance at this time.

It was Ms. C. She had just returned on the ferry. She had come to take a look because there was a crowd gathered here. When she saw it was me, she couldn't help but exclaim in surprise. I don't remember how she asked in surprise at the time, but I took the opportunity to answer and immediately escape the crowd, calling C to walk away. I don't know how that pile of fish ended up. I'm afraid someone still remembers this small oddity.

C was a student of my friend's. I hadn't met her many times before, but she greeted me with such warmth, which I later learned was because my friend often mentioned me. I don't know how vividly and brilliantly my friend depicted my boring and chaotic school life in Shanghai to them. Students in the inland areas often see Shanghai as an ideal world, admiring the modern city, hating the inland areas, and constantly looking for opportunities to run to the city. It's good to be able to go to Shanghai, but if not, they think of Guangzhou or Hong Kong. This illusory ideal often changes a person's character, making it impossible for them to stay in the inland, so they have to go even if they don't have the chance. Naturally, these dreams often shatter, and shattering may not be unlucky, but it's always painful while it's happening.

C's living situation, I don't know if she thought I knew or if she didn't want to say much, she only briefly mentioned where she lived. It was time to go back, so she invited me to sit there, but when she got to the door, she suddenly changed her mind and invited me to see that friend she had mentioned on the road who lived in Cheung Sha Wan. Although I didn't know her friend, because of her strong persuasion, I had agreed on the road to go see her one day. Suddenly she changed it to that day, and I couldn't think of a reason to refuse. So, I followed her towards Nathan Road.

Nathan Road and Cheung Sha Road are connected. They are divided by a cross street, seemingly for no particular reason. Probably just because the following are newly opened virgin lands with few inhabitants. I had never walked this Cheung Sha Road before. C told me it was still a main road leading to the countryside. There was a bay in the middle that was a good place for swimming. We could have gone to take a look, but her friend lived very far away, so we had to take a streetcar. After taking the streetcar to the terminus, we still walked for about twenty minutes to reach her friend's house. In the vast twilight, stood several decaying houses. C walked familiarly up the stairs of the middle one, called out at the door of the second floor. A haggard middle-aged woman walked out. C called her "Auntie," and invited me in with her. The middle-aged woman looked at me for a moment, but didn't say anything. A young man resembling a worker was standing in the hallway, but he dodged into the back room when he saw people coming. C's friend had not yet come out. When C led me into the front room, I could see that she had obviously just finished tidying up some odds and ends.

Probably she was about to ask C who I was, but C asked me first, "Do you recognize her?" This question made me confused. Originally, I knew that we were visiting Ms. L's sister, but at this time, I couldn't help but suspect that C had deliberately fabricated the story, or that it was actually L herself. I couldn't tell the difference in appearance, so I couldn't answer. C laughed, and this L also laughed. At the same time, she seemed to realize who I was. She told me her name and said that she had heard her sister say that I was going to come to see her. Then C laughed again. Probably she was satisfied with her trickery, so she explained the situation of meeting me. She told her that she could learn about my friend's recent situation from me, and also said that I was very interested in the coastal reclamation project, so it would be good to take me to see the reclamation project by the way.

Probably the woman called "Auntie" was busy preparing something in the back. C went to the back to stop her, and then came back to suggest taking a walk by the coast. As soon as we went out, she told me that this house used to be right on the coast, but now hundreds of yards of land have been reclaimed outside. She was very clear about the process and method of reclamation, but she could only speculate about the intentions and methods of the Hong Kong government. This allowed me to roughly guess her circumstances, but I didn't ask her directly, and I didn't ask C about it later. However, C later told me that the worker-like man was L's husband. Their marriage had been arranged since childhood. Neither of them expected that L would eventually accept this blind marriage. She didn't know the situation at the time of the wedding, but she knew that L didn't regret or feel uneasy now, which she always found a bit strange. When C spoke these words, she completely changed her usual lively attitude. Every word she said seemed to carry a bit of pain, making me think that C brought me to see L's home, or was using L's home to show off her own.

Although no one said anything about themselves that evening in Sha Wan, the impression left was very dark, just like the twilight in memory. Ms. L's life was simply like being buried. Her younger sister later became an idolized beauty due to different paths. And the older sister is probably buried in Sha Wan forever. I had a chance to see little L again by chance, but in the extreme hurry, I didn't have time to ask about her sister. And Ms. C has long been truly buried underground. Is the scenery of Sha Wan still the same?

A Certain Train Station

Tokyo Communication

Impressions of the Tokyo Autumn Art Exhibition

— Fang Xun

After arriving in Tokyo, the autumn art exhibitions have unfolded before us with a kind of inertia.

The autumn art season is usually centered on the "Teiten" (Imperial Art Exhibition), but this year, due to the dispute over the reorganization of the Imperial Academy of Fine Arts, the exhibition has been postponed to next year. Therefore, the "Nika" (Second Section Society) exhibition, which was originally considered "unofficial," has taken the lead in this art season. On an afternoon that was as gloomy as early winter, I walked through the Ueno forest and took a turn in the not very crowded venue. Here, please allow me to presumptuously quote a sentence from Heine: "I want to avoid as much as possible criticisms of technical strengths and weaknesses. ... It may be more meaningful to simply write a little about the themes and meanings of these paintings." (Heine: French painter)

Speaking of themes, it seems that a newspaper review said that the characteristic of this year's "Nika" is that the themes are relatively broad. In addition to stereotypical nudes, still lifes, and suburban landscapes, it has gradually begun to seek "cause and effect" in the various aspects of city life. But I want to add that in addition to these various aspects of city life, and very much in line with this "extraordinary time," Japanese painters have already begun to "seek cause and effect in the various aspects of colonial life"! Examples that can be readily cited include Shin Kurihara's "Summer Lama Pagoda," "Summer Manchuria," Jiro Fujii's "Weaving Factory" and "Vegetable Seller" set against the background of Beiping, Kaoruaki Yamao's "Woman with a Natara Pot" with a South Seas theme, and Seigo Taguchi's "Opium Smoking Picture" (two works), "Watching a Play," Tsuguharu Fujita's "Wrestler in Beiping," etc. This shows that although Japanese painters, as Heine (cited above) said, "are far removed from and separate from serious social movements," they have not yet "recognized the uselessness of their cooperation" (of course, the aspect of this cooperation is the opposite of what Heine is referring to)! Secondly, we feel that the surrealist works that have historically dominated Nika, which want to beautify this ugly world and indulge themselves in this beauty, have gradually cooled down, and even from their point of view, there are few noteworthy works. At the same time, what we find interesting is that these writers can strangely still see a gradual transition to applied art. As for the established masters, such as Tokusaburo Masamune, Tokutaro Takaoka, Saburo Miyamoto, Ton Shimizu, ... we can only say that their technology is becoming more and more consummate, but on the contrary, they are also "gradually losing boldness and strength"! Masamune's "Waves," Takaoka's "Woman," and Shimizu's "Sleeping Mother and Child" are all masterpieces of this year, but they only dazzle our eyes with their masterful brushwork and colors. Of course, these works will not give you any sense of the pulse and excitement of the times. By the way, this year's Nika selected many works by Chinese artists, especially the works of Kim Hak-seong (three pieces) and Jiang Zhimin in the sculpture department, which have won considerable praise. However, when I passed through Room 6 (Sculpture), I don't know for what reason, Mr. Jiang Zhimin's somewhat ancient-style headless male statue was being displayed in front of Yoshitomo Watanabe's "Japanese Sword"! This is truly an accidental satire.

Watching a Play

— By Mr. Seigo Taguchi

Three Aspects of Women's Appearance

— By Mr. Saburo Miyamoto

Debt (Continued)

— Zi Gang

Like this, my debt was also built up high, spreading in all directions. I still didn't have the patience to wait for this disease to slowly wear away. I cursed my unhealthy body, in the dark night, in the deep night. I was unwilling to pour the money that my friends had also gotten with difficulty onto the disease. What's the use of fertilizer for a tree that has already rotted at the roots?

My debt collector is my life. I no longer cherish it, no longer try to keep it, with the mindset of "killing it off"!

However, I breathed again, I recovered.

I was able to walk slowly, to step out of the threshold. That ray of blue sky was a stranger to me, a miracle.

My friends congratulated me with kind smiles. At this time, I suddenly remembered: My responsibility is coming!

There are still unfinished debts coming! Although I'm not a shameless rascal, this ray of blue sky and a piece of cloud darkened the leaves of my heart again.

I work, I plod through the streets and alleys again.

In desperation, the big "Pawn" character on the white wall on the street caught my listless eyes, my savior!

However, I didn't have the courage to look around at that high counter.

"What else can I sell?" I often turn over the two messy boxes, calculating how much debt there is, so I tighten the belt and save, and scold the five months of illness fiercely.

At the same time, I think: It's still fortunate to have debt to borrow. In this world, there are tens of thousands of people seeking loans without success. Who do you blame?

Debt saves people, and also forces people to death. The threat of the world is expanding before my eyes. (End)

Ancestral Shrine of Brother and Sister

— Wu Rangsan

Many love stories circulate among the common people of Guangdong. In the simple narratives of the farmers, some are tragic and moving. Regarding this, a friend named Liu Li, who wanders through various villages and county towns, knows a great deal. Once, to encourage a pair of timid lovers, he told them the story of the "Ancestral Shrine of Brother and Sister."

Usually, when Liu Li talks about the customs of various places, I can almost touch with my hand his genuine love for the people of those villages. His love is vast and universal. Without concealing any personal preferences, he loves everyone, without distinguishing between the intelligent and the foolish.

The story begins at Yugu Hill along the West River.

Beside the river in that village, there is an ancestral shrine of brother and sister. The villagers deeply respect and boast about it. The shrine is dedicated to a pair of cousins, the male named Yu Qing, and the female named He Mingzhu, both from the same village. Thirty years ago, they loved each other passionately, but their fathers held generations of hatred and were constantly determined to destroy their dreams. He Mingzhu was the leader among the female singers, but after a hearty and satisfying singing session with her beloved, she was confined by her family.

At that time, the village elders became anxious, worrying about what disasters might occur; the young men went mad, because someone had taken away their idol. The Yu and He families were wealthy and powerful, each harboring an equal number of thugs and storing an equal amount of weapons.

A shocking news spread from the darkness, Mingzhu was pregnant for the first time. Mingzhu's father convened a clan meeting at the He ancestral hall, and he himself proposed to put Mingzhu in a pig cage and drown her in the river, and he personally carried out this cruel punishment.

Yu Ming refused all persuasion and sang a lament by the river for three days and three nights, then stabbed his cruel father with a dagger. To avoid a senseless and tragic armed conflict, he found the place where Mingzhu was drowned and sank himself. No one dared to go into the water to retrieve them, nor had anyone seen their floating corpses. Except for the songs, they never left a trace on Yugu Hill. … The story ends here.

Among those who listened to the story, the washermen A Han and A Xi smiled with a strong expression, and in intimate joy, they merged with the free souls of those two ancient southern barbarians. The timid lovers: the male's monkey-like small face was excitedly flushed, his eyes turbid and flickering, lamenting his own insignificance. The female was completely entranced, as if she had lost her sight and hearing, paralyzed and motionless.

Boileau on Poetry

— Wang Renshu

Recently, I read a Japanese translation of "The Art of Poetry" by the 17th-century French poet Boileau, and I found some of the points to be quite incisive. Originally, this is a famous work that arose from Aristotle's "Poetics", so saying that there are some incisive points here might seem a bit disrespectful. But my meaning is that some of his words can be used as criticism for modern Chinese new poetry, and they are very insightful. Generally, any classic book that makes people happy must have two reasons. One is: "It deeply resonates with my heart." The other is: It can satirize the "fashions" for the reader. I like this book of poetics for the second reason. The Japanese translation of the poetics has a good explanation of Boileau's thoughts, which I will now excerpt and translate:

"This book has four chapters. Half of it discusses general lessons (Chapter One discusses literary lessons, and Chapter Four discusses moral lessons.) The other half discusses the style of poetry. (Chapter Three discusses the three major styles: epic, tragedy, and comedy. Chapter One discusses various short forms of poetry.) Except for the first two sections of Chapter One, which can be seen as an introduction to the whole book and discuss genius, the whole book is permeated with one spirit. What is this spirit? It is the respect for reason. Looking first at Chapter One, the focus of the entire chapter of more than two hundred lines is the following two lines of poetry, “…Love reason! The works of you gentlemen should always borrow their splendor and appearance from reason.” (Section Three) The following seventy lines or so (up to Section Ten) are all elaborations of his doctrine of reason. Avoid seeking bizarre ideas, avoid falling into redundancy, avoid monotony of style, respect elegant taste, pay attention to the form of poetry; these are his main points. … But what exactly is the reason (also called good sense) that Boileau is talking about? Here we should think of the influence of Descartes' philosophy on Boileau's aesthetics. For example, Boileau often says: There is no beauty outside of it. This is entirely Descartes' idea. Because Descartes said that beauty is a form of impersonal reason. However, Boileau's reason is not the pure reason of Descartes. It is a mixture of the modern progressive Cartesian reason and the timid ancient respect for thought since the Renaissance. … Originally, Boileau, just a fastidious citizen, could not have the lofty reason and spiritual independence of someone like Descartes. His reason is somewhat hesitant and humble. He would rather love elegant and upright poetic qualities than unrestrained poetic style and profound poetic beauty. … Boileau uses the alternate name of "good sense" (meaning good judgment) for reason, and he believes, just like Descartes, that good sense is "the best distributor in the world." Under the name of good sense, he vigorously promotes the naturalness and simplicity, perfection and harmony of art, and vigorously promotes the imitation of antiquity. This statement is the statement of the entire French classicism. His contribution lies in combining literary thought with Descartes' theories, giving it a philosophical foundation, and strengthening the foundation of classicism to facilitate its spread..."

This section of explanation gives us two impressions. Boileau requires the fulfillment of reason in the content of literature and art. In its form, he is a classicist. Such a book of poetics is bound to be considered too square. Perhaps some will say that he is a Western "Way-Bearing" faction. But in reality, when I can't understand the impressionist poems written by some people, I would rather recite the ancient poems of "Way-Bearing" people such as Du Fu. Leaving aside the form, I feel that the content is also more solid. At least those people have deeply experienced life. I don't understand inspiration very well. If inspiration can be interpreted as a poet's response to things, then the poet should always have a personality to respond to things. Personality is probably the expression of consciousness (perhaps it can be said to be reason). Then Boileau's words have a basis. And for poets who advocate writing "naturally" poems, it is not without benefit. He said: "Whether you choose an interesting poetic subject, a sublime poetic subject, or any poetic subject, be sure to make good sense always harmonize with rhyme. Although these two seem mutually exclusive, rhyme is subservient. … Under the yoke of reason, rhyme becomes obedient and submissive. … You gentlemen love reason! The works of you gentlemen must always borrow their splendor and appearance from reason. Many people in the world, entirely because they are born with a blood that lacks distinction, often seek their poetic thoughts in a direction far from correct knowledge. In those bizarre poems, if the thoughts contained in them are thoughts that others can think of, they will think that they have lost their reputation. We must not fall into such extreme heresy." He also said: "I am afraid that a shortcoming will instead fall into a big shortcoming, which is often the case. For example, in order to avoid a certain sentence from being too weak, it is made stiff; in order to avoid redundancy, the meaning is unclear." Although these are all very ordinary common sense, they are also the most difficult things to achieve. At the same time, he also said that writing poetry must be popular. In Section Seven, he said: "If you want the public to like it, when writing, you should change the tone from time to time. If the poetic form is too flat or always monotonous, it is useless no matter how brilliant it is. It will definitely put the reader to sleep." He also said: "In poetry, it is fortunate for a poet to be able to shift from seriousness to gentleness with a light and harmonious voice, and from humor to severity. The writings of such a person are loved by heaven and loved by readers." He hates those who write poetry as a game the most. He said: "No matter what you write, never fall into vulgarity. Even vulgar-style poems still have considerable character. Only shameless playwrights, who despise good sense, first deceive the eyes of others, with novelty and cynicism. From then on, the world only sees vulgar illustrations, and the grammatical violations specifically denounced in poetic works are completely unrestricted." Here he condemns affectation and vulgar contempt. What he requires of poets is reason. What is reasonable is true. In Chapter Three, Section Five, he said: "Unreal things can never be seen by the audience. Of course, sometimes real things seem unreal. But unreasonable strange things have no charm for me. People will not be moved by things that even they themselves do not believe are real."

Looking at his poetic theory as a whole, it generally does not go beyond the following points. First, poetry must start from reason, abide by moral lessons, and not teach people to do evil. As in the fourth chapter, he shouts: "Writers, gentlemen, please listen to my instructions. If you gentlemen write works with rich imagination, and want everyone to love reading them, then your poems should be rich in good lessons and often accompany the solid and useful with the pleasant." "The minds and behaviors depicted in your works should show the noble posture of your character. If in poetry you do not know shame, lose your reputation, and write about things that violate virtue with deep guilt, making readers feel close to evil, I do not value such a dangerous writer at all." Therefore, even for inspiration in poetry, he believes that it must have good sense and reading as its foundation. (See Chapter Three, Section Twenty-Six) Second, poetry must have an orderly form and sonorous rhythm. In Chapter Two, he is entirely discussing the form of poetry. At the same time, he also said: "It is not impossible to skillfully choose harmonious words. Any full poetic sentence, noble poetic thought, that cannot be pleasing to the ear, will never please people." Third, in terms of the atmosphere of poetic creation, he advocates being happy rather than melancholy. He said… "Everything in the work should have yang energy! It is not impossible to write poems that are solemn and happy at the same time. I dislike poems that are sublime in any way but show everywhere suppression and heaviness."

Although these arguments are already very old, I still feel that they can be used as fair criticism for the current Chinese poems that are overly flaunting novelty and taking ordinariness as shameful. Let us listen to his words one more time to conclude: "The heart of a daring poet is full of moments of intoxication, wandering in a dreamlike and trance-like state, and he cannot help but break the rhythm of his melancholy feelings. However, it is critics like those described above who can teach you to enter the rhythm well again after breaking it."

Supplement to the Local Edition of Shen Bao

Talks

Regulations on the Prices of Subsidiary Currency in this City

— Meng Ruo

Recently, in this city, on the one hand, rumors have been spreading, and speculators have been manipulating prices on a large scale; on the other hand, the Ministry of Finance has promulgated emergency laws and implemented a new currency policy, causing the prices of various goods to rise sharply one after another. Even subsidiary currencies in the monetary system, such as dimes and copper coins, have also risen sharply. Two weeks ago, the exchange rate for silver dollars was about 12 dimes and 400 cash per silver dollar, and copper coins even reached 3,420 cash. In the past two weeks, dimes have fluctuated between 12 dimes and 200 to 300 cash, and copper coins have hovered around 3,340 to 350 cash. Recently, however, there has been a sudden drop. Each silver dollar can be exchanged for a maximum of 12 dimes and a minimum of 10 dimes and 240 cash, and copper coins can be exchanged for a maximum of 3,000 cash and a minimum of 2,800 cash. As a result, the market has suddenly become chaotic. This has a very significant impact on citizens' purchases and sales.

The prices of subsidiary currency in this city are usually unstable. Even on the same day, the exchange rate for silver dollars varies from exchange shop to exchange shop. Whenever special events occur, it becomes even more unstable. As in the recent situation, the soaring prices of dimes and copper coins have their own reasons, but the manipulation of speculators also contributes to it. Even exchange shops take the opportunity to hoard goods and increase or decrease prices at will. This not only easily causes disputes in the exchange of silver dollars, but also greatly affects the lives of citizens. In recent months, the high exchange rate of silver dollars has caused general small business operators to complain constantly, because the sale of goods is generally calculated in small silver coins. Recently, however, the price of silver dollars has suddenly plummeted, with each silver dollar falling by as much as one dime. This is also sufficient to affect the lives of residents.

In response to this market panic, the silver and money industry must consider how to stabilize silver dollar prices. It is said that yesterday the money market issued a notice stating that, according to the instructions of the Minister of Finance, from the 4th of this month, the price of subsidiary currency will be restricted to 12 dimes per standard currency unit of one dollar, and all exchanges must be carried out at this price, with no increases or decreases. This approach is excellent. However, it is still worth paying attention to whether the exchange shops can implement this regulation consistently in the future. As for the subsidiary currency in this city, it would be our hope that it can gradually become stable due to this change.

Neighbors

— Jia Ren

The family of the bamboo basket maker, Old Woman Shi Lou: the quarrels and fights of four or five sons, the man's crude and violent nature, and Old Woman Shi Lou's own gossiping, shrewishness, all put together, simply become a swarm of bees that incessantly harass the neighbors from morning till night.

That big group of them, father, sons, mother, and daughters, all seem to be evil karmas from previous lives, now hitting each other, mutually demanding repayment of debts. When they meet, they never have good faces. The husband is a coarse laborer, full of savage strength. As soon as he opens his mouth, it's "Your mother this, your mother that, poke your ancestors," spitting out all kinds of filthy words. But Old Woman Shi Lou isn't weak, letting the man curse her as he likes, keeping her mouth shut and not daring to respond. When the man acts like an ox, she also puts on a tough attitude to argue back.

"Bastard seed, may you die a bad death, always insulting other people's ancestors, what kind of talk is that?"

"Whore's nest, dog's breeding, who told you to follow an old man, you worthless slut, unlucky, you still dare to say you come from a good background, heaven knows."

Old Woman Shi Lou is most afraid of people bringing up that matter, because her husband died just two years ago, and the man she's with now is from a secret affair, and also because of this, the neighbors all see her as a promiscuous whore, and no one can stand the sight of her. Yes, other people use this to ridicule her, despise her, and she can't do anything about it. But her husband should cover up this point, yet that scoundrel Shi Lou has no good intentions and is completely devoid of conscience, and instead grabs it as a handle, and whenever they quarrel, he brings it up in detail.

Page 16

He digs at her even harder, and insults her more. Old Woman Shi Lou still has to save face. Although the bad deeds of the past can't be hidden, she can't help but get angry when her husband deliberately touches her scars like that.

"Stinking bastard, if I'm a whore, then you're a turtle, you can say that too."

The veins on her forehead swelled up like earthworms, her voice rising higher and higher, yelling like a broken gong.

That man Shi Lou, is indeed a man with a heart of stone. When he sees the woman's appearance, he doesn't show a trace of pity or sympathy. Instead, his anger flares up even more. He glares with his eyes, smiling sinisterly; and while gathering strength, he rushes over, grabbing the woman's hair, just like a fierce tiger snatching a small rabbit, and then starts beating her with his feet and hands.

Old Woman Shi Lou falls to the ground, struggling and cursing, and crying and wailing.

The sounds of the beating spread out, and the neighbors ran in one by one to watch the show. The onlookers have no feelings, just find it interesting. It's that same old thing again, that same old thing has really been performed countless times.

Shi Lou is equally disgusted with the onlookers, and has no good feelings for them. When he sees more and more people, he roars:

"Damn it, get out, there's nothing to see here, you grandsons of tortoises."

The onlookers all glare at him and disperse bored.

In the eyes of the neighbors, Old Woman Shi Lou's fate after remarrying is considered deserved, because a woman who does not abide by marital fidelity will naturally have no good ending. The suffering Old Woman Shi Lou endures is precisely the justice of heaven, the punishment she deserves. Besides, that man was already a no-good person, he drinks, causes trouble, gambles, he has all the bad habits of idlers, and once he drinks alcohol, he goes home to vent his temper on the woman, which is enough for the woman to suffer.

Why did she have to follow such a rogue? It's all her own doing.

Early on, the man opened a shop specializing in selling bamboo baskets, and people called him Brother Shi Lou, and the woman was also Old Woman Shi Lou. Because Shi Lou was useless, muddling through life, and didn't want to do any work, the shop closed down a long time ago. Later, he worked as a day laborer for farmers. But doing day labor has a fixed time, it doesn't last all year round. Plus, his bad reputation is known far and wide, and gradually no one dares to hire him.

A family of six or seven people, of course it is even more difficult to support themselves, so fighting and arguing are almost daily occurrences in the ears of the villagers.

Besides the awkward couple, the four children around the age of ten were all brought by her from her previous failed marriage.

When there was nowhere to turn, Shi Lou turned his thoughts to the children.

"Sell those little devils, make a few dozen dollars and be done with it."

With the alcohol in his stomach, the man said firmly.

"Heavens, you should die, you've eaten everything, you even want to eat your sons."

"Who are my sons, turtles' breeding."

The woman has nothing to say, just lowers her head and sheds tears.

Driven by livelihood, there is no way to go, so selling the sons is the only option. Selling sons to survive, the villagers almost rioted, but they ignored everything outside, and then another one was sold, and Old Woman Shi Lou seemed like a prolific sow, having a son every year, having one and selling one, and now they are probably still raising and selling at the same time.

After Old Woman Shi Lou dies in the future, she will surely be thrown into the eighteenth level of hell, made to climb mountains of knives and enter oil cauldrons to be punished, the old people all say this.

Musings on the Weather

— Hu Si

Wind

Last night, a strong wind blew continuously, and the trees outside the house sounded like a heavy rain, and the doors and windows kept making soft sounds as they were blown. Looking out the window, the weather was strangely gloomy, and dark clouds filled the sky. There were no pedestrians on the road, and the streetlights were dim. A kind of unspoken sadness was immersed in my heart, the world seemed strangely unfeeling, and life seemed a little tiresome.

As for the wind, I never seemed to have felt a sense of loneliness. I have also drifted far across the sea. Although the ocean's strong winds are frightening, and I have been trapped in the boat, lying down for three days and three nights, it did not make me feel disgusted. Instead, when the wind and waves were slightly smaller, I struggled to get up and look at the sea view, and seeing the waves rolling with white flowers, and feeling the ship jumping in the waves, was even more beautiful, and it caused another kind of pleasure. On other flat sea voyages, seeing the sea as flat as a mirror, without a trace of wind, and no wrinkles in the sea, I would feel that it was completely meaningless, and my taste for and love of the sea would decrease because of this.

When I was a child, I encountered a great disaster of wind. Trees were uprooted and houses were knocked down, and many people and animals were lost at that time. The sea also roared, the sea water flooded the land, knocking down houses and sinking ships; that wind was so strong that it could blow a person away: from the land to the rivers, or from the roof to the ground. But I was fortunate enough to escape the disaster. I only remember that at that time, my family all lay on the floor under a solid wooden bed, and my mother held me tightly, as if when the house was blown down by the wind, we could also be saved by the strong bed board. That night, the sound of the wind was shrill, like ghosts howling, like a group of wild beasts roaring. The beams of the house kept cracking from time to time, and the thick wooden door of the old house was撞得阵阵地在响被风撞得阵阵地在响by the wind. My father and mother's faces were gray, as if a great disaster was about to befall them, and they made trembling conversations from time to time. But I was wrapped in a quilt, embraced by my mother, and didn't feel anything scary, and sometimes I would even sleep soundly for a while. When the wind stopped in the morning, I saw a blur in the suburbs. Some trees were broken, some houses were collapsed, and the whole thing was a blurry gray and white world. Although a sense of desolation would also arise in my childhood heart, I vaguely let the impression go.

Ten years ago, I stayed at the house of a friend by the sea. That night, because old friends gathered, the friends talked very happily. Everyone drank a little wine, their faces flushed, and they talked about everything under the sun. When the night was quiet, I heard the roaring of the waves, and a strong wind swept from the sea. We even had the interest to pick up a flashlight and patrol the beach. Seeing the waves spraying directly onto the shore, almost wetting the bottom hem of our trousers, everyone laughed and jumped for joy seeing the sea all dark and a hazy night constantly showing Qing-white. The wind was so fond of us young people!

The breeze in the rubber tree forest in the South Seas is even more beloved by me. After the scorching heat of the long days, being able to rest in the forest, or take a walk after dinner, blowing the wind at dusk, and listening to the Malay love songs gently passing through the wind, is very pleasant. If it is by the sea, it is even better. The wind of the sea is fresh and sweet, it can intoxicate people, and it can also make people dream. The taste of this kind of sea breeze is really hard to taste in other places.

Therefore, in my past life, the components of love for the wind are more than the components of dislike. But once a person passes middle age, they feel that their mood has changed. Last night's strong wind, accompanied by my insomnia, made me sink into gloomy brooding all night, just like gloomy weather. Constantly listening to the roar of the wind, constantly listening to the sound of the leaves swaying, I also sighed, and a kind of inexplicable boredom and depression expanded with the sound of the wind, and my mood was like being blown by a strong wind into the vast sky, inexplicable. I used to not believe that the weather could change a person's mood, but now I believe it. But will I feel sad because the lively spirit of youth that has been ground away by life? Or will I rejoice that I have gained something from the experiences of life?

Tiger

— Ji Tuan

Life is like a fierce tiger, it constantly opens its big mouth, strikes a predatory pose, and watches me intently, ready in the moment of "one carelessness among a thousand cautions," to tear my chest with its brutal claws, and to suck all my blood with its rough, sandpaper-like tongue.

I don't know when, life lost its beauty for me and settled around me like a constantly lurking beast. Day and night, I felt like I was in a desolate mountain, facing that terrifying beast.

But, so be it, it's a beast! There's nothing to fear from a tiger; if I want to live, I have youth and courage, don't I? At that time (but I don't know when that was), I used to think that way. So, I began to smile at the tiger facing me—smiling so proudly! Like a confident hunter, overly confident that he could subdue this ferocious beast with his bare hands, making it a display and reward for his labor—"A newborn calf fears no tiger," as some people say, right?

I said, "I am standing in front of the tiger (if life is really a tiger). I want to see how it tears people apart piece by piece; I also want to see the inevitable final result: either I kill it, or it devours me. It is not my master, but must be my slave!"

So, I saw its cruel predatory actions: and I also saw this absolutely irreconcilable result! That result! I was afraid, I lost all courage to think.

Yes, what's there to think about, what's there to say? Morning and night, sitting blankly, reflected in the mirror is a withered appearance, thin, pale, and gloomy, like a low-lying area in a valley, where the smiling sun will never shine—contemplation, labor, running, endurance, for many years, I exhausted all my energy to deal with the tiger's claws, it gripped me tightly, tighter and tighter: and I myself felt more and more tired and exhausted, I gradually began to feel its power—constantly缠绕me, threatening me; so, day by day, letting its claws sink into my flesh, letting its rough tongue touch the numerous wounds: I will be torn apart and sucked dry—definitely!—Now the worst result has come: that is, the tiger of life has become my master! A supreme tyrant who likes to see people's struggles as the best dance, who likes to use other people's blood as a substitute for sweet red wine.

Aren't the roars enough to make people tremble under the claws of life? Life is not a small matter; it's a terrifying thing, as fierce as a tiger, as tightly缠绕as a python. Countless people are rushing about under it: people get tired, people's smiles disappear, people get old, people die—lying quietly under the ground, but with a cluster of indelible tiger claw marks on their bodies and in their hearts.

Perhaps some people still think their youth is something to be proud of? Yes, be proud—when you live among the teeth and claws of a tiger-like life day by day, you will cry.

Now, from a confident grasp of life, I have been left with a lifetime of beast claw marks. It's like being branded, forever indelible. I know that one day I will be torn to pieces and devoured by this tiger—and that day must not be far away, definitely not far away.

Once again, I trembled.

Song Introduction

Modern Girl

Modern girls, afraid to get out of bed in the cold, with drowsy eyes, emerge from their boudoirs after noon, delicate and languid, waiting for their willow waists to be propped up, leaning on the sofa with tea, designing elaborate makeup, painting eyebrows and applying lipstick, with faces as white as frost. Imported goods, greasy with fragrant powder, sisters, enthusiastically promote them, willing to transport the blood of compatriots to foreign lands, look at the machine guns in their hands, all are gifts from modern girls. Alas! Sadness.

Modern girls, hating long days of painting in the heat, call friends and companions, busily making phone calls, electric fans humming, carefree and happy, enjoying cold drinks and chewing white ice, yawning lazily, exposing chests and arms, enjoying the evening breeze. Cicada-wing skirts, unrestrained forms, sisters, lighthearted and unrestrained, making appointments at the movie theater, intoxicated in the dance hall, forming the appearance of fallen willows and remnant flowers, all are the brewing of modern girls. Alas! Heartbreaking.

Plum blossom, though not the king of flowers. Is noble and outstanding. From ancient times, poets have praised it. The reputation of flower leader is unparalleled. I don't know that the plum is both hermit and gentleman. With a virtuous nature, high character, and dignified appearance. People in the world mostly praise peach and plum. Peach blossoms are charming, plum blossoms fragrant. The plum blossom. Only seeks stability. Unwilling to be fashionable, learning new makeup. With extraordinary elegance and no vulgarity. Ashamed to compete with peaches and plums for fragrance. Without a good matchmaker. Also without harm. The fairy of Miaogu is originally without a partner. Mountain friends are pine and bamboo. — Zhi Er

It is said that the Electrics Bimonthly will be published separately, and Zhao Gongbang is said to be in charge.

"Les Misérables" Publicly Screened in Nanjing

The greatest literary creation of the year by United Artists 20th Century Company, "Les Misérables," is now being publicly screened in Nanjing. Its original author is the great French writer, poet, playwright, and novelist Victor Hugo. This immortal treasure has been translated and spread all over the world. It describes sad life, cold cruelty, slaughter, etc., which is indeed heartbreaking. The two great artists who starred in the film, Frederic March and Charles Laughton, have shown their acting talents in blockbusters such as "Resurrection" and "Min Yuan." In short, a great work has its own undeniable greatness, and intelligent moviegoers will be able to appreciate this artistic crystallization and give it the value it deserves.
